Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	In some cases, you should make three or four cautery marks along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cauterization we mentioned earlier; and do not press your hand against the entire cautery, and let the hairs be close by on its back; and another method of cauterization is to heat the cautery that has two needles, as we showed in the shoulder dislocation; and lift the curtain that is near the mouse's ear, where the pain from the hairs comes from the right side, and let the elevations you lift the curtain according to its curve, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After boiling the two needles for a while until the tips are perceived from the other side, then remove the caustic, and thus enter into one it will have four. And if you see, then cauterize the entire caustic with three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has gotten gout by being too long, and this is worth mentioning that the other treatments mentioned before should be done.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Caustic is not good for hydropsy, except in the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the spleen, and one behind the back above the spine, and one in the worst place; and let the cauteries be very close to the surface of the skin.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cauterization, allow it to heal for a long time, and do not neglect the care of the wound after the cauterization; and healing will be hastened, and together with the help of God, the two intentions will be achieved.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the fire cauterization for the abdomen is like the one we have shown before; and for the back, it is like an olive branch, according to what is written above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen to the one who is hydroptic, and are plain of wounds yellowish, it is necessary that you cauterize above the foot between the auricular and the anular; and lift your hand with the cauterization towards returning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, thus avoiding the yellowish part, and let the cautery be done in this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. de la menoison	of the minimum

When the solution of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and the intestines are blocked, and cannot be cured by other methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great pain, then make a large cautery across the stomach according to what has been said before or a cautery of the stomach, around the cauterizing circle; and four incisions around the subtle belly at all the subtle clavile, and two incisions on the hips.

Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the cartilage that is called "thelul".

When you cut the cartilage, if the fire burns like a razor, and then put it all on top of the cut cartilage; and let your hand go as far as the cauterizer comes to the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much cartilage, cauterize each part as we have said; afterwards cure the wounds until they are healthy; and if you cauterize with a large fire on top of the cartilage, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the wounds cannot be treated by a surgeon or opened up, as we will tell in its place, then the disease comes that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any fistula comes and is swollen and oozing pus and corrupted moisture, then you should apply a fine tent all over it, and make sure that you remove the tent as much as possible.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cauterizing iron that seems like a razor, and putting it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and then start the cauterization again until the wounds are cured and corrupted are destroyed, once, or twice, or three times, depending on the amount of damage; and beware of burning the nerves that are in the way, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the center of the bladder and the intestine, do not attempt to cure it except in the case where it is immediately visible, and think that it is not healed; after curing the wound as long as it is healthy, and if the wound is open, the matters are removed along with the tension, then wash that the wound is completely healed; and if the matters are not removed, wash that the wound is broken, and corrupt the bone at the source; and thus as one of those that we will say in its wound.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	of the marsh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the groin of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the muscles of the buttocks are found to be displaced, it is necessary that you cauterize the injury above the groin of the hip with a cautery similar to a circle, and sign before the joint around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and if it is such a cauterization as those which have been cauterized in the stomach.

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the misalignments are cured of what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the disease is ancient: therefore it is necessary that you purge the misalignments of heavy humors with fetid pills, or other good-quality pills similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is thus: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cauterization.

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then make two cauterizations where the pain is located, and one cautery at the ankle four fingers, on the right side a little; and let the cauterizing knife be sharp, and burn off the tendons; and if the pain spreads to the knee or near it, cauterize where you feel the pain three times or four with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If it is a mechanical job, do more; and if the pain is located between the groin and thigh, perform cauterization with a pointed or circular cauterizer, and be very careful in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long, burning nerves and large arteries, and causing greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	I myself have seen many who have cauterized above the ankle bone, and left it on for so long that the leg was completely infected, and the foot as well, and all the bones were corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly that caused death.

Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use this cautery little because of its fearsome appearance, and few see those who use it; nevertheless, it is a good cauterizer, which can bear the pain, and where it is applied.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with lead from a goose, it helps a lot; and it should be done in this way by the cauterizers.

Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre». de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of two days
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from impact or from too great evacuation, or from similar spread cold matter, none of these remedies is as good as fire cauterization, because it is from hot infusion of cold matter.

de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is due to moisture that spreads to each limb of the body, and when pain comes suddenly, which is properly called "gout", and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it should be treated with cauterization in this manner: apply a lot of cauterization around the joint, and let the cauterizing oil be used in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick the face with a needle, then apply the entire cauterization that is called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come from the joints and other joints, and this often happens, then apply cauterization to each joint with three or four needles of each part, throughout the entire cauterization; and if you have more skill, do so, but do not hold your hand too far away until the pain of the patient is relieved.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the joints and back, then administer the cauterization that we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are severe, apply a bandage two fingers wide; and if they do not remain, apply a bandage over each joint and over the hair of the hand; and if the pains come from the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good management to the patient and proper medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good management and purify the blood, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the nose
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the break comes in anger, and the blood flows down to the knees and this is new, if you see it when it happens, do not move it that day; and use things that make the stomach heavy, so that the blood does not flow out of its belly; afterwards, let him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to tilt his head as long as the bleeding is not stopped, and then press them down to his side, and sign over the break above the bone of the wrist, and at all a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cauterizing iron in this way:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it sweats scents.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the mud from the joint; and the ministers tie a cloth over their hands so they do not return; and work well on the thighs at the wound, and put some ointment and some salt on his thighs, and the other on the worst hand that stains the hands; then put the cautery on the sign all over your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again with another one until you reach the bone; and be careful that the mud does not come out when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this way the wounds do not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And if you do not come to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterizer for children be done subtly according to their size, and for large people also according to their size; after three days, care for the leg of the fire cautery until the burn is healed; then care for other wounds until it is healthy, and gently rub the bad parts 40 times on its back until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that its dislocations be stretched long, so that the blisters do not rise when they try to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and let it remain for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and avoid too much repletion from drinking and eating, and too high breathing; and if he follows this instruction, he will be completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of cutting into his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the tearing of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When tears come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, let him have the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let the third part of the cure be applied; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles in this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the shoulder blade protruding and make a line across the width of the tear, and another one below, and hold your hand at all the cauterizing iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, or to collapse or to pierce, and this pain lasts long, and the medical cure does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cauterizing iron called «poins», and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healthy enough for the first cautery, it is good; if not, begin another cautery above that one, as it is often customary to let it die to the member that is closest, because it is necessary that you do the cauteries until the hairs are healthy.
de meselerie	to treat wounds
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Wounds are never treated with cauterization without great help, and at the same time, the disease that comes from the putrefaction of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see that the wound is being cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the previous section, and does not deteriorate or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the wound, then make the following cauterizations: I apply the cauterization to the head towards the front; and the other to the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and II on the two corners, and I behind the temple; and leave as much space as the cauterization comes close to the bone, and until the scabs fall off so that the vapors of large humors can escape; and cauterize again according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	If the fracture is scattered everywhere; and it is obviously present, so you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and the cauterant in the middle of the nose, and two cauterants above the spine of the neck, and six cauterants above the spine of the back, and one great one on each side of the buttocks and one other below, and two above the shoulders, and two above the elbows, and two above the knees, and one above each joint of the hands and feet, and above the wounds of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the calcaneum, that you do not burn them; and never make any cauterant above the bone of the little finger, and one above the bone of the stomach, and one above the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the more you perform cauterization, the less help it provides; and the more it benefits, and the less painful it is for the patient as healthy people experience, because the body is already corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the limb with flour multiple times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then perform cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization go slightly into the skin; then treat the wounds until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never cauterize by hand, at the palm, or at the back, of the nerve that moves the limb, thus it becomes stiff and inflamed; and otherwise, no one should meddle with it unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and their movements.
de albaras	And never cauterize by hand, at the
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and medical treatment is of no avail, then cauterize with a cautery a little in front, according to the amount of the cure's courage, until the flesh is stiffened and turned its color; then treat with flour of wheat and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and salt of colon and salt of almond, each a part; and mix all together, and apply to the affected area, and bandage with a cloth, and keep it on the body until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stop spreading, if you cauterize it with a cauterizing iron that seems to be in the shape of a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the sages say that one should also make a cauterization in the middle of the chancre; and I do not think this is good, because I believe it will not be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen only once; and the better thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cauterizing iron that is called «circle», as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflamed part that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati", and it lingers in dying due to the excess it causes or because of the old age when they are too old, and they have little blood, or because of the tension; then you see it hastening to die: therefore cauterize around with many small cautery needles, pricking; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced by the whole cautery, then heat the cautery with which this is shaped.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced through, and be such cauteries that the hairs feel afterwards in a similar manner as the course of the pustule is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until they are completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a piece of member, for it bends the members as if the dry reeds did.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb that can suffer cauterization together with fire, then heat the cauteries with a very small and great flame, according to what is necessary for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply a cauterized cloth on the wounds, suffering with oil until the scars of the fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds, burns arise.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy burns do not arise, it is good; but if not, then reapply the cauterization on the remaining wounds.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method has never been treated with medicine in place of fire cauterization; but nonetheless, fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the cure of medicine ague in the division: take it when you have the opportunity.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of peas that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, it comes to the feet through defecation, and a disease arises that is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a great thing that becomes large in the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries of this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to say, fire cauterization, and water cauterization with hot iron.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is that you heat the cauterization as if it were a pen of feather, and it is made of good iron at the measure that it can penetrate the nail on all parts, and that it has thin edges; afterwards, put it all hot above the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the end of the nail; and leave it in this way for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment of wild herbs ground with silk, and leave the ointment all night, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out by its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with heat, applying hot poultices until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by previous injuries to the body, and often in the hands and feet, then it is necessary to apply cauterization with very hot iron; and it is done in this way: take a needle of iron or steel, or a pen of vulture, and place it on the nail and the cuticle, that is, the dead skin; then place the needle on so that it pierces all around, then put a drop of very hot water, and hold your hand tightly, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the needle reaches the root of the nail, and find the very hot water deep to the root; and let the patient feel the pain of the very hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will fall off at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do another one after that, until you have relieved all those that are in the chest, then treat the wounds that engender fire.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of the tremor
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold or from intermittent fever or other, it is necessary that you make four cautery burns or four above the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the chest, and one above the stomach at the cautery oil; it will leave the trembling, and hasten the healing of the disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No times appear from before the body is bathed, or pustules arise, which come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary when they appear that one make a fire cauterization above each head of the pustule: a subtle fire cautery of birch wood, of which the point should be grasped in the fire, or of the root of aristolochia long, or with the lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And no times cauterize at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and it cannot grow new ones, but is broken down the excess from which they come, and are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there is great loss of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes from the surrounding area, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, quickly place your finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very tightly until the bleeding is stopped from your finger, and no more blood comes out; then heat up the cauterizing irons in oil several times as large or small as they are all red; then take I, or great or small according to the wound and the limb where the artery is located, and put the cauterizing iron on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterizing iron until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you lift the other end of the vein quickly, and the cauterizer is extinguished, then take the other cauterizers that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the wound; and watch that when the artery is cut, if it cannot be stopped immediately when the artery is large, it must be done in one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cauterizing, or by extracting it when it is not yet treated, or by a strong thread, or by medicines placed on top that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be tied and held tightly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the tightening of ropes or other things burning above, or similar things, does not profit unless they do not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no present remedy, they should put their finger index above the wound of the vein as we have said, and well tighten until it is tightened above the wound and above the vein; and they should not move it, but keep it cold often until it is frozen and swollen and tightened; and make inquiries in advance about what they have to do with cauteries and remedies.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of remedies for tailors
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with a burning medicine, and the symptoms and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I will put this chapter of the shoulder joint from head to foot, and I will go through this same way in order to find more easily what we want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore when I begin this chapter, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come in cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such people who are so with their disease that they die immediately because of the harm they find in their disease, and the greatness of its wickedness; and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these, there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not enough that you allow those who come to you who have this way, but put more caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not open rashly but wisely of what you are certain, and what you have taken and lost; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your diseases for health to be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory for long.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords grant you good understanding and truth, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of her hand, indeed.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered you to read this chapter by comparing it with other chapters on cauteries, as I have explained from the beginning to the end, so that you can find out more easily what you will need to do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of sharp
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often occurs in children when they are born, and when the child's head is held too tightly; and sometimes it comes because of a sudden movement that cannot be prevented.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease except in children, and to all those I have seen it has been fatal; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to avoid this work in treating them.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child who was suffering from a sharp pain, and the head was swelling each day until it could not bear it; and he thought so much of the moisture that he died, and this moisture is gathered outside the bone above the shoulder joint, between the neck and the bone; and the remedies are such that if the moisture is between the neck and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a wide cut into the head; and it should be as long as our thumb, so that the moisture flows out; and take this shape of the sponge:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more severe, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is outside the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the joint open on each part, and the sharp pain when you press with your hand inside, and it has not been relieved: then you must make three incisions in the joint according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain all the moisture out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After closing the incisions with dressings and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and let it rest for five days; then remove the dressing, and cure the wound with poultices and counter-irritants, and keep the joint immobilized, and gradually reduce the moisture by drying the meat with a little moisture until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look for the opening of the abscess, and the gathering of the sharp point; for it is never in front, never behind, never on the right, and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess is open, and fill it with the sharp point, and make the incision according to what you can do; and be careful not to cover the artery; and if blood flows, then the wound may die due to the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	return
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the pupil, and the disease is ancient, and the medical cure does not help much, then the treatment is cauterization with what is used to cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you see the hairs covering, that the hairs make their head; after that, he rubs the shoulder with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then he holds the hairs back against the cloth; then look where the blood comes out, and the veins on both sides are near the ears, and they are not replaced; then sign the veins of the cheek, then cover both with a piece of cloth of two parts, until the wound comes just to the bone, and it should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, push the piece of cloth away from the artery and cover it above, cutting in the same way as it should be across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood should flow continuously from it.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pricked, it is necessary to measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then make an incision down to the bone; and what amount of sinew is needed to put out, is six centimeters, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on how much pain the patient can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone pointedly, if the pus that has been removed does not come back, then strain the wound and tie it, and the treatment of the ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	de emigrainne
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient emigrainne comes, and the cataract is active, due to the moisture of tears and the chills in the forehead and old age and similar things, and it is treated with methods of medical cures and nothing seems to help, then we should cauterize the arteries of the forehead, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is that the hairs of his temples are made to stand up, and one listens to the artery that opens in the forehead, because it opens well by its beating, and it is pounded only in some people who are too fat; and if it is pounded, then one strains the skin with some cloths, then rubs the skin with some rough cloth, and raises the skin with hot water until the artery opens clearly; then take the spatula of which this is formed:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then slightly scrape the thin skin until you reach the artery, then cut it upwards with pincers, and remove all the threads that are stuck to each part; and if the artery is very thin, turn it back to the tip of the needle, then cover that part according to the amount of the two chapters.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the sixth vein, just to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong silk thread, which does not allow any blood to come before the healing of the wound, and prevent the formation of pus; then cover the excess between the two knots in the same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the wound with the cautery knife up to the bone until the chapters are covered; and this is the final work, if the wounds do not have fever and he is of hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery, it is helpful to finish the moistures: because it is the greatest help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and place dry bandages on top; and when they are removed, care must be taken with dry medicines that produce heat and bandages, as long as they are clean; and if there is no copper present, you should apply the wound with vinegar and the bandage to your hand that the wound is not stuck; and if you do not have this present, you should apply ice to the wound until it is frozen, and raise the wound with cold water until it is clean, and hold it as it should be; and what is more difficult and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting from II parts, but the cuts should be well spaced to last longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When instruments are too tight, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a gap of large space, and then when you have marked the two lines, and you melt the hot iron above as far as it comes near to the bone, and cover the vein in two lines; and they should be separated between the two cuts because there is no safeguard from this cauterization altogether; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from veins that are above the testicle of the head, and it does not profit much from medical care, and you see the face of the evil becoming twisted, and feeling as if trembling; and they are held and moist so that the hairs of the papers are soaked, and the papers are stained, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is a need for this care.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old "wound healer," and you should make three cuts or front evenly according to the length of the front; and one of the cuts as two completely in the front by lifting up and down just above the neck, and the others two on each side of the ribs, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on each side of the ribs; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and for each wound the quantity of three drops through the joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then suck the wound with the mouth in two parts of which this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is to be made from the temple just above the second incision; and scrape off everything that is between the two cuts up to the entire face which is above the bone, then make another part of the same incision just above the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "curette" into the first cut, it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not very sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp edge of the instrument towards the surface of the bone, and the soft edge towards the bone, and the cut as far as it comes to the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cover all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is continuous up to the point where the curd opens, and then do the other side in the same way on the other side; and then extract the pus equally, and express the wound for the pus taken; then put in each incision a piece of old cotton, and put on bandages moistened in wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure that abscesses do not come; and the patient should apply a large amount of salt on the wound, then the care of basilicon with rose oil, and other remedies that are used to cure wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	return of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any come to have the fire cautery as usual, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakened in sight, and the papers burned; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done there is pain, and the hairs are blocked; then by these accidents those matters and that fire do not come from a single vein, and the cure that is, if this is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a great cut across the forehead, and another one wide at the top of the nose.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins from the wound of the right temple to the left temple, and let the incision just touch the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in the mouth; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood onto a sponge, then clean between the two lips of the wound and put old cotton, and linen; then bind it with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against pus forming; when it is taken out, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to appear, then treat the things that are used to draw out charcoal.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of collophane, and make an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to inject charcoal throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which pierces into the ears is one of the four things: either grains or bone or stone or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or something flowing such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it pierces into the ear or in another way of thing that does not fit well in the ear, it does not grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see an arrow, if any drops of purple oil or hemp oil are distilled, then apply extraction; and the effect is to make him spit out the condition, and stop his nose when he sneezes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around his ear; and place the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, apply extraction with fine pricks, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the fine pricks, that is good; if not, apply extraction with a thin needle; and if it does not come out by this, make a tube of rain and blow into the head of the tube or the hole of the ear very hard so that nothing can enter with the tube; then pull it out properly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take some thread and wrap it around the ears, and put any instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton inside; then press the thread on the arrow or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly pierce the ear as soon as an abscess forms and bleeds, and spasms; and the manner of the piercing is that you first make a small incision into the painful part of the ear, and extract the pus according to its strength, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the grease hangs; and let the incision be as if it were a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck vigorously into your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small and swollen, administer extraction; and if it cannot exit, then administer the following subtle form of spatula:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make a mistake in thinking that the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract with delicate forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of something lodging in the ear, it is recommended that the hairs be blown out first with a conditioner, and then cleanse the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie flat on the ear itself or where the sharp is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps up for heaven's sake, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your finger and light ones, and heat them in the fire; and put the hairs one or two at a time into the ear, and step on the other part of your foot, and strike with another stone above the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this stone after stone until the sharp is all out, and thus it jumps out all out; and if you see, take the splint, and boil one of the stones in the ear, and the other stone take from the fire as long as the thickest splint is ready; then make the other splints as before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the animal, if it is of small size, such as a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel, then ameliorate the extraction of pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the division and if you treat distillations, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with fine pincers, and if there are none, take the cauterizing iron of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And the most subtle sharpness in the ear according to the amount of pain, then it often goes all over the body; do this frequently until everything is visible.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to go out, then dull the pain around the body as I have said in the stone; and if they cannot bear it as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have discovered in the treatment of wounds, and you will find them where treating distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with this instrument, then the form is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or lead, poke them out of the small pores and above with a spout; and to press within the distillation, use a well-made instrument of lead for this purpose, and if you see the razor and wrap it around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the can, and the can should be in the ear; then press through the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or slowly from the ear; and the smell of the medicine inside, and it should be the distillations are slightly heated on the fire as when it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear deafness
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some deafness in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by ear deafness, or by a bone inside the ear, and this deafness never comes from anything inside the ear, if one cannot see it; and it always comes from something outside the ear, and one sees it well.
