Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That deafness which comes from something inside the ear, if one cannot see it, is due to great inflammation in many positions, and in this one, where one sees, one must put the ear on a bad side towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacity throughout this space of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the hot iron move back and forth over the entire surface, so that it does not burn the ear; if the opilation is of charcoal or horsehair, then hold it with fine pincers, and the copper gently, until that charcoal is completely burned.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is placed inside the ear, then take a fine razor and slightly heat it over the fire, then put it on the horsehair of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opilation that causes the patient to feel gritty in the ear, slightly cut, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the pustule, and moisten it with Egyptian honey.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not use the joint for any activity until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with strong rose water, and powder it with broken glass; and if you see inflammation in the ear, it is advisable to remove the tent and apply another one made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak an sponge and apply cold cloths on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding of blood which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of the book
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the process of drying the bones that come from paper when they are wet and are dry, if it is necessary to stretch them with tongs and pincers, and the root of a spatula from its roots; then place on the bone vitreous glue.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without removing them, the cauterizer with the subtle lens-shaped fire, and the cauterizer after the incision is good; and often they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the powder
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Frequently arrive in papers certain things that seem grainy in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail", and it is an assembly of moisture large on the paper above and below; the workings are such: if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape each part slightly, then take it with pincers, and the cope.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a slight perforation in the paper, it does not hurt the patient; and if the force is great, it assembles at a seam, and the cure until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the wounds restore quickly and inflame.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the sharp bone is falling downwards into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the sharp bone in some forceps, and hold it with a cloth and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it does not hurt anything; and when the sharp bone is cut off, pour some oil of strong salt on the wound, and heal the limb as soon as possible until the painful parts are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is squeezed out of the threads of paper above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes much, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears stick to their eyes; and for this reason they lie on their faces and sleep on their sides, and their papers are outside their heads moist with the exinach that has puffed up and covered them.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint to your touch and feel the extrusion between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains extrusion from each part, then place it on top of it; and press from one side and the other, so that the extrusion is assembled within the circle; then make a small cut in the middle of the moisture at the sharp spatula, and not more than the size of the wound on the vein; and make the skin even until you come to the extrusion; and in many positions of the extrusion from the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the whole piece of cloth that is between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to insert into the wound, that you do not come to all the oil just above the skin, that you do not damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, gently rub the wound until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then wipe cloths in hot and cold water, and put on the limb, and bandage well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break the cloth and put it on to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the body with an abscess that is open, then the healer applies wet dressings until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born that are not natural, and are awakened, if they harm the eyes, and bring on diseases such as tears accustomed and softening of the papers and whiteness, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in four ways: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine wet, according to what is before or chapter of cauterization, and is done either by incision and sewing or by needles, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the badly positioned part in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is an needle at the end of the thread; and so it is on the other side of the paper, over the hairs that grow from these hairs, and pull the thread above the paper, and return it to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the skin painted, from the great leg to the small one; then pull the thread, and place on the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of an envelope, like the fuller's mallet, and in all cases it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you saw lifted the paper that is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is a matter of someone who has skill in coping with great quantities of paper according to the way the paper is softened; then make all the space above the two lines that you have marked, and beginning at the large arm from great to small; and let one of the slits near the hairs in the growth of a root, then squeeze the thread into one of the two angles of the needle, then scrape off the skin; then bring together the two lips to a seam of an needle at all the thread of fine silk, and wipe the blood, and make the excess hair above the two edges to any things gluing, if you see to do this; and if not, if you have no care, then leave the seam and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without sewn things, dry and constricting, because the paper re-lives at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is dried (as they said the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if in another way: and that you sign the paper in a shape that is as alike to the form of the mirror, at three threads according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply heat evenly according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or there is a thread, and put it in the shape; and put the other thread over the big arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have told, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and never once has the hair of the paper been converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of the dogs is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the thread inside according to what I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two subtle links as long as the paper and the breadth of the oil is; and cope with the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly above what covers the paper of the oil, and strain the two dogs from the two parts formed; and leave it thus for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off through it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the copper has strong forces, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been dressed, and if the paper has been lifted, and the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two cups that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and pull the silk thread softly and thinly; then assemble the hairs and both subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly, and do not twist the other thread; then put the hairs on your skin so that the work is shaded, for this is a delicate and small work, then pull the needle through the entire work at the root of the pricked hair, and push it through the paper gently until you remove it from the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the work, and push in the work that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out of the entire work with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the bone is treated and the hairs do not come off with it, then you should treat the bone with the fat that you have ordered, as long as the bone is still fresh and you can see it through the oil; then you should apply the fat and leave it for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows on top of it. And if the hairs are small, then accompany them with a long hair from a goat's tail, and raise it with the other one until it is lengthened and then let it go.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the appearance of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "gout", comes into the oil, there are two methods: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by injury of wound, or by cutting or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this is that you break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put in tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and you should only use in its care things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease becomes worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the root of a sharp or high plant and seed of linseed should be cooked, and an ointment of turpentine founded in any of the oils, and there is wrapped in a tent, and the care of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your knowledge are that you take care that it does not decay according to its former form; and this work that we have said is only a preliminary to this disease, that it does not return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the jar
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axiocratic", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the method of this work is that you hold an needle, in which it has a double thread, and the thread in the jar, and you make it pierce from the right arm to the left, so that the thread comes out of both the holes of the jar; then the jar is placed above the entire needle, and the cloth wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the paper fits according to what it should be, it's good; if not, take the razor and put it in the groove, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or at the edges of the incision you have made; and let the corners of the two cuts be such that when they are assembled, the shape is as much like the shape of a letter that has not «I greek»; then remove that char, according to the amount that its cost is away from, what the paper means, then add the two missing parts, and the cure of what we have said about softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.

If the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain cut outside of the hairs and papers, according to what has been said before; then squeeze between the two leathers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the wise masters apply various means to help bring back the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is needed of work and instruments in many ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	doubtfully of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil

des voines des eulz	of the eyes

de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil from the sinus.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	from the oil and pain
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez. dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a silk cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the silk cloth, then open, and come forcefully like grains of resin, and is unpleasant to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you should stick a needle into the root of the part below the arm above, then stick another needle or where the double thread of the arm is; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the double thread of the thread around the part of the wound, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and put some soft oil on the wound, and let it stay until the thread cuts with the wound, then care for the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never the wound is bandaged by a piece of cloth from each part of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly affected, prick them with a fine needle that comes from under the skin, and draw out the moisture and wipe away the pus, and apply this immediately; then extract as much as is necessary until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from under the skin
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called «alcunnati» is nothing more than a swelling that is assembled under the skin, resembling a sharp, descending arrow, but it is not an arrow; and the way of its appearance in the work is such that you make the pain sit on the seat, well-dressed and straight, then take the chief between your hands from both sides, and move the muscle until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it go, and do not wipe off and do not dislodge it, and see the things as they should be; and if it does not disappear, then it is an arrow, and if it dislodges from the swelling, it is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the painful part is placed between your hands, then take the thin spatula and place it under the corneal thread and gently pull on the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal thread and the crown, until the arrow is released; and when it is released, then pour hot oil mixed with honey, or hot oil or fenugreek boiled with honey, then let it be treated with other treatments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have experienced similar cases in the division, and what is needed to pierce; if it works according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the dislocated joint rest between your hands crossed, outside of the light for the sun, and with clean and tightly stretched oil; then place the oil paper at your right hand if the joints are crossed, or at your left hand if they are uncrossed; then take in your right hand if the joints are crossed, or in your left hand if they are uncrossed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your right hand if the joints are uncrossed; then place the point of the almagda above the crown of the oil at the thickest part of the elbow, then press the almagda virtuously, and restore your hand as long as it pierces into the crown of the oil, and feel that the almagda is coming to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda be at the front of the measure of the space that is from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the canvas, and then place the instrument above it or at the sharp end, then extract one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he sharp now sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if he sharp raises the second vein, put the feather with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, gently rotate your hand around and around; then place a small piece of silk gently into the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place by default the stuck oil or cotton soaked in red wine and plenty of vinegar, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on top with plenty of vinegar.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arrow cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctive, and do not move it too much, but make the eye soft, then push the arrow as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the patient's sleeping position, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and avoid all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie according to his disposition just after this time; then remove him from this same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then return the bandage on the seventh day; and you should not do this in the early hours of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise the eye, because the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply a poultice before the seventh hour, and appease it with what quenches abscesses; and when it is calmed, remove the bandage and put oil on its face to cover any wound, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then slowly and gradually leave the dark house, and return to your own home; and let no one interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who was in the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people practice archery, where the arrowhead succeeds the arrow, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read any in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almada, because those who do not know them see them thus; and they are of pure rain:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the heads of some from this same subtlety, and the rest in three angles awake.
de la char sor le neis	of the char for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do they ever arise or grow from the nose, of which there are some that seem like scorpions in size; and if there are such ones, or if there is a swollen wound of bad color, and if there is a soure wound of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those wounds which are soure and not swollen, it is necessary for you to place the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the onion juice to those wounds, and pull out the pus; because it is as if you could support the subtle sting of one part, until you know that that wound is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is anything remaining that cannot be removed, open it with all the subtle and delicate instruments until nothing remains; and if it is an abscess, apply hot compresses as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the wound is not soaked and all the pus is removed. Then pour out or cleanse with vinegar and hot water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not heal, and moisture enters into the palate, it is because it is infected; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, it is because there is a bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting properly. Therefore, you must go inside with a thin piece of linen, and hold it with your hands, and leave some space between each thread; and put the bad parts of the thread into the wound through the mouth, and pull it out until it comes out through the mouth; and many times they do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it; then hold the part that comes out through the mouth with one hand, and the other part that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them together as we have shown.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the newt is not corrupted with that cloth, then remove the filament, soak the blood, and moisten the filament in Egyptian wet compresses, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the wet compresses corrode all that remains of the newt; then place or put a plug in the nose for several hours until it is healed, and if it needs medicated oils, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, shaped like an open lamp, such as a plug, and use it in the same way; and if you see, make a closed plug, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the fire cautery
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Frequently, a disease arises at the base of the nose called "telul", which grows and becomes large over time; and because of this, it is necessary to cover it from the beginning, and to remove all the furrows, then place the fire cautery or the burning medicine on the affected area; and if it is difficult to cover it completely, if it is hard, of poor color, and without sensation: if you do not touch it with iron, because it is a hidden abscess, for when it is covered, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is softly touched, not hard, and you see that it can be completely covered, then remove the abscess and cover it without fear, and cure the affected person of similar and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bones are cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	For solutions in continuation come from one of these cartilages, which is of little use, as in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound has no bone, look to see if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then bring together the two lips at a seam, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already rotten on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scorch all the parts of them until they are healed, then bring together the two lips at a seam, hold it in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and frankincense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and leave it until it eats through him, then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is such that you gather the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have shown to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses inside their lips, which are hard and small or large; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips and cut under each tooth, and take them with pincers and rub in every part; then apply the wound after the incision of broken glass, until the wound is not stained; and then apply a poultice, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a toothache arises from the gums due to a cavity, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary that you support it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let out the pus or the blood; then put on the tooth with vitriol powder broken into pieces, or other astringent and desiccating powders; and if the toothache returns after the incision, and often does, then cover it again and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never are gathered at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the teeth, sharp instruments which are disgusting and sharp; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the tooth, and they are foul-smelling teeth. Therefore, you should make the patient sit the pain between your hands, and their teeth in your holy place, and clean the teeth or the sharp instruments wherever they appear, until nothing remains; and thus remove the blackness and greenness and yellowing and other stains, as long as they are cleaned. And if you remove what is at the first level, it is good; but if not, then start again from the second day and the third tool, until you have removed everything. And know that the teeth have a matter of various forms of instruments to clean, according to what the work demonstrates, because the razor with which you clean the teeth has different forms than the one used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay pulling it for as long as possible, for one should not do this; for it is a substance very high and thus one has no excuse to pull it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the pain is constrained to pull the tooth, you must be certain of the tooth hurting.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the tooth is deceived, and one must be sure it is a holy tooth, and pull out the good tooth; and then the pain does not depart, until the evil is extracted, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are certain of the tooth hurting, then it is necessary that you burn around the tooth at all points; then move it with your fingers or subtle forceps at the first and second point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly fix the forceps; and let the one with the pain in your holy mouth between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump back, take one of these tools and gently push it into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulps are; and if the straightening subtly has a crack, that it does not break when being pulled out; and it is very important to cover around the gum to relieve the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and again cause the patient great pain by the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant physicians, who by their haste and boldness break the chariots every time, and do not remedy what we have told; but bring about great disease from the roots that they delay, or from the chariots that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the bone is drawn, wash the leg with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows, use the leg often with vitriol broth; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long pointed and large-handed, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large-bodied so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be pointed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, it is necessary to put a moistened cloth on the wound or two or three.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so long as the wound is softened, then pull the forceps called "algefri", of which the patient seems to have a sharp edge; and they should be made inside like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out at all these needles, then it is necessary that you dig around the root completely, and put the tool called "althali", which is a spoon, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be large enough so that it does not break into pieces, and if the root jumps out of the ground, it is good; if not, with all the tools, of which these shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this tool that has two prongs, of which this shape comes:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the range of the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large needles, of which this shape comes:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be used only when it cannot break, and sharp that many tools of dense are; and also other tools, which are not mentioned here; and the wise masters find their own tool by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach any tool for the diversity of them; and if they have broken the chariot or other bones, or if it has caused harm, if they search for tools that are needed, as I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but he can hold and remove; then restore the limb with appropriate medicines according to this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if the surgeon has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot be a dentist or limer; then the ray; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument from which there is the shape, and it is similar to the small beak, and it is made of iron sharp at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth becomes increasingly painful over time due to its hardness, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the tooth is extracted with a tool like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the tooth of which arrows are made; and in extracting the tooth, one gradually moves it over time, so that it does not move until it breaks; then, at the end, with any sharp instrument, and if the tooth is too deeply embedded and bleeds the tongue, then one must extract the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they pull out teeth
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when they pull out teeth, either by pulling or by hammering, and the patient cannot press up against the pain that makes them want to spit out what they are holding in their mouth, and you treat them with tightening medicines, it does not work; then you should restrain them with a gold wire, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never does; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are moving, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the sick tooth between the other teeth, as many times as there is one or more, until you feel firmly against the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering towards the part where you started, and gently and firmly press your hand, so that it does not move at all; and let your thread be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the broken teeth with a thin wire, and gather them together, and place them between the healthy tooth and the gum, so that they do not bleed the tongue; and then leave them thus tightly as long as possible, and if they dislodge, or the wire breaks, then use another wire; if they remain, and serve in this way throughout their entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the reattachment of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth cracks, if it is reset in its place, from small to small, as we have said; and it does not interfere with anything that is wise and suffering, and never once made the shape of an animal's tooth, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is there a fracture of the jaw that comes from dislocation of the tongue or naturally, which one is born thus; or by accident of wounding; and the works are such that you cover the mouth with the tongue, and hold its head in your own, and lift the tongue; then cover the nerve of the jaw with a wide cloth, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if it is hard or does not move, and this is due to wounding, if you boil the wound and cover it with a wide cloth; and be careful that the wound is not too much in front, for the artery which is outside; and when you have done, lift the jaw of high rose and vinegar, or high cold water, then remove the tongue from one tent of linen; and treat the wound with vinegar every night, that the wounds may not stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If there is bleeding from an arrow, put a piece of broken glass on the wound; if it does not stop, cauterize with slow-burning charcoal, which is good for the flesh; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the wound is of a dark or black color and hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is chancre; and if it is discharging pus and there is moisture, pour it out, and put a thin sponge underneath, and deliver it from both sides; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, place broken glass on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you remove all the blood; then lift up the limb and bandage it, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There are no abscesses in the throat that are called "godath", and they are properly called the II mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is an abscess hard of small size and of brown color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the escape of blood; but let it be so long as it is alive, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check that the abscess has settled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit with their back to the sun, and their injured side facing upwards, and the operator's hand on their shoulder, and press the tongue away from all the instruments, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all these instruments, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and the needle in the amber, and draw it out above as far as you can; and take nothing else with, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, which seems like a forceps; and all the chief are curved, and one end the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if it is shaped like a pair of tongs, with this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And it should be shaped like tongs on one side and flat on the other; and when you have taken hold of one of the tongs, take hold of the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cold water, and if there is blood coming out, gargle the sharp pain with hot water, or use pounded green pomegranate skins or mint leaves, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then treat the cure as long as it is healthy; and never any other abscesses than the two tongs are born in the throat, so take them then like the two tongs should be.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I treated a woman with an abscess that was closed within her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the condition she was in, and could not eat or drink, and died if she remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been placed with two needles through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore acted quickly, and pierced one end with a needle, then I removed a large portion of the abscess; then I refilled the other nostril with another needle, and I pushed the tongue out of the mouth; afterwards I pierced the other end of the abscess, and collected a part of it, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman's breathing was restored to her, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew again and filled the cavity that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I pushed it back in and cauterized it within her throat: thus she did not grow again; and I left those parts and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it comes to the eye, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not too large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you should cover it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red or black, then you should avoid the incision of the.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	When you see it, as I have said, according to its length and width, you should place the painful part in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then cut the incision in the vein, and draw out the blood, and bind it with one or two of the instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you only bind as much as the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you bind more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two arrows, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is not too great, it is recommended that you use a device for the cauterization of the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cauterization is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your shoulder, and then presses the tongue against the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and applies with very hot fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and while moving this instrument, which has the following form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head has a hair or object that one uses to apply the medicine, like the movement of a spoon, and places the instrument on top of the medicine over the tongue; and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down the throat and into the lungs; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it over the tongue for half an hour, until you see the medicine is effective and the effects of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through the cotton into the throat, until the cotton burns over the tongue; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days, and if you have to restart the cauterization of the medicine, start again, and after the cauterization, wipe it around the tongue with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be covered with hot water, and be treated with gargles until they are healed.
