Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from the incision than the cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in a pot, and put in vinegar, and make boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the prongs stuck in the patient's mouth until the steam rises to the ulcer through the gum, until the ulcer is dead; afterwards, repeat often, until the ulcer dries, and guard that you do not make steam at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make steam except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cloth and put it inside the head, so that the tongue does not stick out too much; for the cloth does not cause the vapor to burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, it is necessary to remove bones or fish spines from the throat, or nothing at all; therefore, you must remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open for you and is returned to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit the thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is removed by vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes back to the throat, it will stick, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instruments be bent at the head so that they can more lightly enter into the throat, and have the head raised high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that the whole does not come, or push in the bone; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, for it is softer or the thing is as such; if it goes down, or it pulls it all along the instrument evenly, as long as it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinew
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	The throat sinew is never treated with medicine as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the throat of the pain to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, then cut it at every small notch, or with fine needles that are worth the use.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not hold, then take a hairy cord, and push it into the throat of the patient, then push or move the cord with the sharp iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient's wound becomes infected all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take plenty of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it down their throat, and move it with your hand often; and if as soon as the sinew feels the cold, then stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not cough as we have said, then smoke the bad breath of asafoetida with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of onions; do this many times, for it will eventually stop.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you hold a pot or where there is charcoal visible, and place it in the middle of a cover, and in that puncture the patient with the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the bad breath in their mouth, and close their mouth, so that the fumes do not escape, but go just to their nose; and the nose will now clear up, and if she does not cough, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient fast, and give them things that are salty and other, and do not let them drink any vinegar; and thus it is the matter that they will be cured by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the shoulder is, when it can be seen, similar to curved hooks entering the throat; and it resembles a beak, and there is a roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip. And this is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscess, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that one is in its own form, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are at the neck.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the neck are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is dead according to its completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, as abscess that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and one leaves it until it is swollen inside, perhaps the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which it is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located away from the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located away from the base, if you pierce it too late, it will not be able to pass through, and will remain inside, and there will be a fistula; and it cannot be healed in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to remove the pus from the abscess that has died according to the completion of the drainage, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the swelling, and the relief and the easing of the main abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the drainage wherever it depends from the abscess, and where it opens into the muscle; and it should be the longitudinal course of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the throat, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it beforehand, it may spread along with the blood of the vein, and is stained with much feces; and by chance it hardens the lips and penetrates deeply into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured according to the width of the vein, according to what the limbs have to do.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you incise small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the cure, and to cover; when it has become as soft as cloth, and is dead, then it is necessary to do as one does with bubbles: and if there are such abscesses that are cut in three angles, and if there are such abscesses that one covers like the flank of a mule, like an abscess of an angle; and if there are such abscesses where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the abscess is superficial, it is necessary to puncture it completely; and when the abscess is large, and has much pus, and you puncture it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only part of it; then treat the abscess again the next day, then draw out nothing else; do this repeatedly many times, until all the pus is drawn out; especially if the wound is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced should never once with the issue of the pus, that by chance the wound dies, and you do not lose it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, suck the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small; and if a tailor complains, alleviate the pain with linen or woolen cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you fill each one with old cotton or rags of linen without moisture, and tie it to the wound; then open, and treat the dressing until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your work, apply sharp cold and wet compresses, and wipe the blood, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply government and care, and the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is not too tight, and if the wound or abscess is very painful, then you should put on tents and wet cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a state of inflammation, and the wound is charred, then you should put on wet cloths soaked in cold water and oil, or warm wine and oil, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress it and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally about the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or when small abscesses come from the head, and are like those that are in cloth, as is the joist of a girl's skirt, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that have moisture like chickens; and there are some that are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the belly is such that you should try all instruments called "intestinoscope", from which this thing comes about.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it does so through the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off anything that contains that moisture, for it will remain in place if left alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it there the next day; and this will prevent what remains from lasting longer.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with an ointment suitable for its condition, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess does not yield quickly, then prick it according to this form, from the long side; and pour in your pinpricks, and scrape off all parts of the skin, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is located. And if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat the abscess if it is piercing, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And on the abscess above the bone, if it is soft and watery, it is less bloody because it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and if they are like the ones I copied from an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard and rough and white as a stone, and could not break it; and if one had tried to cut it, one would have made just as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses, it is because those that come from the top of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made at the lowest part of the joint, to let the pus out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscesses at the neck, and remove the tonsils, and then anger, and sometimes come from other parts of the body, and are very large, and are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and each tumor is properly within its own side, as with the one and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these tumors are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and if there are malicious ones that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that one then that you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar to the color of the blood, and moves from each part and is not near the neck nor the artery nor the conduit, and is not deeply; then it is necessary that you cut through above, and scrape every part, and set the two lips of the wound as evenly as possible, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that it is not too narrow, that the hand does not escape, and does not see too early, that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not stop bleeding, pour into the wound vitriol broth, or some powders that stop blood, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is healed, and begin to sew.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then examine your patient to see if there are any small pustules remaining, and cut and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the pustule, it is not advisable to cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through it, without causing harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scab, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound, and hold them in place now, as there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you cover the root of the tooth with a material and draw out the pulp, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that remain excessively should be pricked where the pus is most abundant; and prick them in this way, hanging down, then apply ointment and similar things, so that they do not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply charoite ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I have never seen one in our land, and this is the written record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the furrow of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and this cannot be helped because all the veins and the pore of the evil are in those who have abscesses greatly in the mouth, or in the throat or in the hollows.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it through three circles or four with a small cut across, between the two circles or by the amount of the cut through the soft tissue, not in the cartilage; and those who are thus suitable for the section of the epiglottis have no charcoal, and their vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary to stretch the skin of the neck all around, then cut the throat until it reaches the windpipe; avoid the blood vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the soft tissue, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the windpipe that flows through the bone that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and close it entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause vomiting until they are expelled.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that we should not do this unless the throat is completely stiffened, and the hairs are judged to be dead, and the defect has healed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should cover the epiglottis for this reason that the hairs cannot support, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they ordered the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four. And therefore, they commanded to sew the wound and cure, as long as it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a dagger and stabbed herself in the throat, and cut part of her windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found that an arrow had come out of it, and although she had not bled much or coughed blood except from her throat, and the blood came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and closed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and she did not die as long as she was able to speak, and she returned to her usual state afterwards; because I believe that in the covering of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a great abscess in the color of a yolk, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or naturally, without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one occurs in two ways: one way is similar to a large goiter, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a small incision in the neck, and the proof and search are made through all the incisions: if you find it as I have described, and it cannot be removed at all, then cover it as one would cover a goiter, and bring it out entirely, if there is any; and examine it well, and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of ours are, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I tell the whole difference between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is hot and feverish, until the ebullitions are passed, and it is accompanied by putrefaction; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With ours there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains the syphilitic pustule, which is its own secretion and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a small spot, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either dry or moist, and much of the color is as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the cure of a patient, it is necessary to first test and inquire about the "entromissoire" instrument, according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiry for abscesses is that you hold or press a moist cloth over the abscess, and gradually pull it back, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the center, then adjust the "entromissoire" according to the size of the abscess; then remove it, and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running wound is moist and has a certain color, make it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after the "entromissoire" does not come out moist, check that it is fat, then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with pincers, and scrape off all the skin from each part and wipe the coat or where it was so that you remove it clean with the patient; and if you cannot remove it clean, then tear it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if it lingers for a short time, and does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, close the wound, and place soothing things on the abscess, and treat other wounds until they are healed; and if it is large, cut out the two lips of the wound, and treat what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it be contrary or other, and you are in a hurry, apply the leg of broken glass, and leave it for two or three days until the wound closes, and let the blood clot; then return to the copper that remains from the blood.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments used for extracting foreign bodies, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three ways: large, medium, and small, to extract the stones of fistulas; and they are like the needles that one buys for sewing, and are made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and cost as much as those that are already yellow, and are more commonly used to extract the stones of fistulas; and they are of three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the fistulas.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are nails with two beaks of three ways; and if there are nails with three beaks, and they are also of three ways; and if there are nails with two beaks, and a single beak nail, and they are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these that we use are sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than from one part, from which we scrape the skin, because we do not want to cut the vein or nerve; and these probes are the needles returned in hand-held form, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and no other instrument is used except in lean places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; and never made any other tool small, resembling the scrapes of pustules, according to this form, for evacuating blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never placed back in its proper place which can cope with veins, and arteries, and never again returns to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like the breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and if anyone wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with a healing charcoal powder, then stitch the two lips of the wound together, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is softened by its great size like in women, and is sewn together in the ribs above, because of similar tears; so that one holds the other at the end of each, so that the greatest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the pain does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with a corrosive cotton swab; and let it remain until it melts the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the ankles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the ankles are hard lumps or with cuts, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is drained, apply old cloth to the wound and leave it until the other day, then remove all the cloth, and treat with ointment as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is an abscess of similar appearance to a scrofula, then make incisions in the same way as we have described for cutting into scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is discolored, then there are often abscesses, and also bleeding from the vein; and if you know that it is due to the artery, then make incisions along its length; and when you feel it with your fingers, it will be painful; and when it is due to the vein, it will be red and swollen; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and angles and chest and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the use of iron and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen due to arterial bleeding through a long incision in the skin; then open the belly with small incisions, and separate the artery from the cloth until it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce the other side with another needle, and tie the artery with a double thread according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not remove the piece between the two limbs of the intestine until the one that is missing has been removed, and if it is an abscess, so it should be treated as indicated, until it is healed; and if it is for the belly, if there is an abscess, so you should dip your hand in what comes from the abscess to all the skin, then remove the needle from the piece that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have indicated, or with one of the two threads of the other side of the needle; and if you doubt that the thread will not fit, then insert another needle throughout the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four pieces; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the excess with the cure and leave what is tied; then place a moistened cloth on it in wine and oil, then treat the wounds and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come to the arteries and veins, and abscesses also come to nerves when they are injured or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And it often happens to the helpers and the doctors in all the limbs where there are joints, and this is the greatest abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many positions with pain; and when one stretches it, one feels the pain, and it is not from the flesh, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not need to be covered by iron: perhaps there will be contraction; and those who are in the head or face, making the skin thin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if it has a head, and you cut at its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it from its base, and scrape it, then remove the bone and assemble the wound at the seam, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is no case in the belly and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "funge" by its resemblance to pus, and it has a subtle root, and large swellings; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or three bellies that were more like funges than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were torn, and it spread with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one weighing eighteen ounces, and in the other six drams, and the work in the incision is such that you should look to see if the hairs are moist, and the color of the artifact is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper is large, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the cutting often comes too great blood loss, and if you do not see the hair escaping and painful from the incision of the iron, then take the thread well made, and tie the artifact as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop pulling the thread through until it covers the artifact, and work through it with effort; and if the roots are large, then use the copper directly on the belly, but you must cover half of it, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thin which is of pale color and poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these are abscesses that have become infected, and I will come to treat chancres afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the body is full of blood
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the fullness comes from the cauterization of a wound or a cut of the syphilitic ulcer, and it is above the belly and in some of the bruises, as it has in other wounds, of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of pus; and if it is from the rupture of the syphilitic ulcer and from the issue of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the end of the intestine, then it is the most diverse, and when pressed at both ends, it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and opens well when pressed with the hand, but do not force much; and if it is due to blood, it is wide open by these signs of abscesses, which are thick and hard, and is like a bag; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the appearance is whether it is for the blood of the artery, or the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be for the intestine or the abscess, then you must command the patient to dye his linen, and let it extend straight all around, then sign around the belly; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the part that you have marked with a strong silk cord, and make sure the intestine is not included; if you find the linen, cut it off, and bring out the intestine from behind the stomach; and if you find the abscess, take it at the base, and scrape away the excess; and if the artery or vein goes against you, go around it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread two pieces of strong silk, and cut the abscess into four parts with the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the part as long as it can bear, and kill the dead flesh by itself; or you can cover it when it has become thin and ready to burst, then cure the part as we have said; and strain out the pus or the moisture that you have found, then cure the part as it needs, and soak the part.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have mentioned in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one must work with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre is engendered in the marsh, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancient one said that when chancre is in a place where it can be removed as chancre which is in mammaries, and in the chest, and in similar places, and one must remove all of it when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, if one does not advise approaching it, for I have never seen anyone heal it; and no one has ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedures, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you remove the hairs once of black coal; then clean it if it has manifest repletion, then bathe the wound in good blood for the procedure; then pour your bile or pus, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow fully, and wipe well the wound with your hand or something, and if the bleeding does not stop, it makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, if it cauterizes until the blood is stopped; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: if it is only swelling; and one should not touch with fire in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for this is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look at whether the pains are weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as vomiting and similar things; then do not touch with fire, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then thus: lift the patient upright over your hands, and the ministers press the belly emptying the sharp to the lowest part of the least, then take the sponge according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them be cut from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cut from the tip, and ensure that no part is cut so thinly that it can reach the intestines when thrown, and cannot be bleached; then check if there is hernia towards the intestines: if necessary, make a cut of three fingers' breadth from the left side of the belly three fingers' breadth above the navel; and if it is for liver disease, make your cut on the right side of the belly three fingers' breadth; and if it is for the spleen, make it on the left side, and do not let the hairs grow over the cut so that the excess does not run to the weak side; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push, and withdraw your hand from all the space between the skin and the flesh as you would when scraping a quantity of an inch or around; then pierce the flesh until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the length of the wound, then remove it, and push this instrument of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or chalk, and has small perforations; and on one side, three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the patient's tail is cut as if with a pen, and that is the shape of the incision that the scribes make to write with the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the awl, so that when the instrument comes to the skin, then write now above the instrument; without the half or the third part, because if you take more than it should be in that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit of the arm, or he throws his hand, or he approaches death; but in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound signify, and its pricks; then take the instrument and retain the skin, and it is retained now for the one who stops the perforation that is above the eyebrow, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering so, and take a small quantity of blood from the skin; do this every day, and guard yourself from following as long as it does not delay but only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and you let it out too much, then the care of the sepulture or sand cures, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if it becomes infected; and the care of desiccative medicines until they are healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the sharp object, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the insertion of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born without a wart on the rod, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce everywhere very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or pierce very thin threads of linen, and bind it and keep it in this way for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if it is not convenient, then remove the threads and let him urinate, and then put them back; because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pierced is small, then it is treated with a thin thread of linen, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the piercing in their own leg are foolish, because no one is born with a piercing at the top of the thigh, so that they cannot urinate before their thigh is raised; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come down to the marris, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie flat on their backs, with the head of the knife and the blade as narrow as the tail of a pen, so that the puncture is made in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding from the wound, which often occurs, and if it does, stop the flow of blood with a bandage, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come cysts in the knife, and it is an appearance of a wound that is ugly; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; if you should prick them with a fine needle, and cut and clean all of them, then put on a moistened cloth in Egyptian ointment; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If it is a bad dislocation, with a putrid color and swelling, then you must apply heat.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have treated it, and if the dislocation is in the middle of the bone and part inside and part outside, then you must first fix the dislocation that is inside; and when it is fixed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, if the bone is not pierced, and it turns black and corrupts in its bone and at the joint; then remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply the plaster of honey and flour that is made from the skins of grapefruits and oranges, then treat other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	If there is bleeding from a wound, then apply the lunar caustic according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two situations together: that is, at the outflow of blood, and in corruption; and if the tail is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary to apply a piece of cloth soaked in urine on the wounds, and piss on the painful parts; and when the hair goes up to the head of the stick which has not been circumcised, or if it is for a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to burn it with the instrument that is at the end of the stick, until the flesh is separated, and deliver the tail from all parts; and if it is a difficult thing to do this, then it is necessary to burn it at the head of the stick and the skin, and then apply a subtle dressing of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not grow back.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our desire, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest in terms of health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and sages who performed circumcision in the ancient times, and they all did it the same way; if there was two threads, and by chance if someone pulled one above and the other below, it could cause a problem.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is complicated, and the pain is doubled, and in the disinfection that is not always sure of the point of the member; and in the disinfection of the finger, perhaps the needle slips and pierces the work, and often they are born such that they have no need of disinfection and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the disinfection that is done with force to the whole length of the thread, I found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut equally as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the thread; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and that the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he listens, that you only tie the thread around the stick as much as possible, and then throw it in all ways that you can; then bring the thread straight between your hands, and hold the force between your hands or outside your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the stick and blow gently, and take it up as high as the part of the stick is ens; then clean it well from the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it away from one end to the other; and hold it in two places by the second work, and cover between the two threads, then lift the gentle thing up slowly and take the head of the stick; then let the blood drip little by little, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on and on the powder a paste made of one part of honey cooked badly with rosewater, confected with rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the other day, and cure the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the mummification is such: the two shoulder blades should be close and sharp, and the shoulders should also be as great as the chest evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mummification is when the knife enters during the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your angle, as well as the copper, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then use nails, and then the copper.
