Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they overshoot three hours, and what is outside the rod is inflated, let it remain until the abscess is calmed, and scrape lightly; and if the copper as you can move, and guard from the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the wound of things powdered plague, that we have said or treat the powders, and if it is dealt with excessive care, and it goes above, it will not harm; cure therefore as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is caused by obstruction of the stone, or of blood congealed, or of bowel, or of charred, or of similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is high or close to the bladder, then it is necessary that the pain be raised above its knees; and its feet are placed on the back, and its belly is stretched from the part above the back, and the pain is restrained as much as possible; and therefore the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it is made of thin silver hair, like the pen of an eagle; and it is made of a palm of a half length, and subtle at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the wool or cotton to the pocket, and push the head of the thread into the tube; and wipe the excess of the wool and push it at the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg yolk, and seat the patient on a chair, and remove the bladder and the wet cloth and oil of olive and vinegar; then press the tube firmly to the end of the tube, until it reaches the base of the tube, then double the tube over against the belt; then push the tube in front just above the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming just above the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conductor or she goes twisted; then stop the thread all along the pocket little by little, and the urine follows the pocket, then remove it, and correct the urine; and start again the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, and putrefaction is present, and you see it drip watery and medicinal substances, then use all the instrument called «clepsedre», and its form is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three prongs: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads by which the medicine is held are such that it does not stick to the urethra too much, so that the moisture can be drawn out, and put where necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the tip of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it to the drawing which is outside; if you draw the moisture to the catheter, and then tighten it strongly outside; the moisture will enter the catheter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel the pain; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: if it is in:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or lead, and is the highest of the chest; and remove from the side where the ribs are broken; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see glueing the bladder, then place it between the two breasts formed by a good piece of cloth doubled, and heat the poultice over the fire; then pour the head of the poultice into the stick, then hold your hand on the bladder throughout the moisture, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then fill the filaments strongly with these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dough, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the section on stones the methods of cutting and extraction along with the medicines; and I have said the difference between a stone embedded in the rain, and all the signs, and which kind of stone one should open with a drill; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder is more common in children, and it is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder, like a sharp sting, is very severe; and if you have a sudden urge to urinate, it hurts greatly, and often makes them fall down; and they are often bedridden, and the cure for children under four years old is light, until they grow up, and it is more difficult for those who are between young and old.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, in order to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never fails to cause trouble when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand it upright and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the bladder, and never once rise above the thigh; then place it between your hands, clean it, and its hands be away from its thighs, so that the bladder is entirely descending down; then remove and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not cough up the thick phlegm at once, then gently press your right index finger on her upper lip, if the pain is sharp, or in the middle, if the pain is dull; and place it on its base, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the back of the neck; then press upwards, and the stone will come out where you see it was cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the servant to press the anus with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand over the testicles, and with his left hand remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spongy tissue, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And making between what is between the bones and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the right nave; and straight up the stone, and your right should be at the foundation, and your left should be at the bottom, and the tail should be across so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow on the inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the right hand which is at the bottom, that it may jump out without effort; and if there are pieces of stone or angles, and margins: if it is grey to be removed; and if there is a piece which is soft, like a glove, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When it is in such places where there are angles and margins, make the incision wider; and if it does not heal, then you must strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from slipping out; or you can use a subtle hook bent into the shape of a head; and if you cannot engage it in this way, then enlarge the opening slightly, and if there is no bone, then strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, then first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the rest, and the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be cut to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it kills, or the urine comes out where the legs cannot sew together; but nevertheless you try to pull it out, or tear it apart with pliers, until you tear it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply encaustic and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bandage it, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and vinegar and cold rosewater, to alleviate the abscess; then replace the wound on its collar, and do not leave the bandage loose for too long.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, if it arises very well from the joint of oil and vinegar, then treat it with ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by the urine, which is known in a similar way as without leakage with the urine: then put your hand on the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and ruin it; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and olive oil, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you cure it with, that you tie the two thighs together, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the arrow is small, and it is conducted with a stick, and tied up, and the urine cannot come out; then as I said before, that you cut many times, or excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three corners tied up in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the arrow around the stick outside the wound, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then lightly hit the iron on the stick until it reaches the arrow; and slowly turn the iron in your hand into the arrow until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; if the urine comes out immediately, then press your hand above where the remaining part of the arrow is inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is already broken, and has sprung with the urine, and is sharp against the bones; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then make the rod at the right place between the two threads, then extract the thread, and loosen the bone, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is rarely a stone in women, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who will undress herself specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's, because it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, you should send for a wise and experienced midwife, and if you cannot find one, do not proceed with the operation, but rather cast the net widely; and present a skilled woman in women's affairs, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and look closely whether the woman is virgin: then it is necessary to place her on her back and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she should remove it outside her body, and recommend that she place it in a jar or with pain, and press her right hand firmly over the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the body where it is muddied and covered, and feel the arrow in that part; and do not move her arm above the bone or below, and let the tailor make a small opening in the wound, if you feel the arrow so sharp that the wound can be opened wide enough for the arrow to come out, and know that there are many ways of arrows: namely, small and large and sharp and blunt, long and round and rough and smooth, and those with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know it, put the similar piece of glass in the wound, and keep it there for an hour until the pain is gone; then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have the tools that I told you about in the extraction of the stone to help you in your work; and if you do not know it, and it is the artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bandage it with tents and bendels, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient might die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound is closed, then return to your work, until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	For hernia, follow this procedure:
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white sphacelus, which is outside the curd of the cheese, which contains the whey; and it is called «sphacelus», and never is properly in the cloth of the whey, if one wants that it be another whey; and this does not exist unless not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is due to weakness that comes to the curds, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes if it comes from percussion on the teeth, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or watery white, and there are more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white and facial as we have said, it is the abscesses, and not long since like the figure of an egg, and does not open the teeth, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own cloth, it is the abscesses with part of an egg, and because one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the teeth and the white facial, then it feels good; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try all the surrounding parts, from which the form was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes afterwards, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When we treat it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to how much power and the replenishment of its body; then place it on its back, on something a bit high, and cover it with much cloth; then lean on its right side, and command the minister to lean on its left, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the kidneys; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the kidneys from long to above the knuckle, and make your incision straight in cutting the skin of the kidneys towards the white face, and scrape the skin subtly according to how much power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp and wide cut, and extract all the sharpness, and then put your forceps, and fix the white above; and do not touch the kidneys except the white itself; cover everything or even in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, if you do not cover it well, it will return to the sharpness; and if the wound opens up in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white. Then gather the two flaps of the kidneys at one seam, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the wound infected with another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cover the wound with a bandage, and extract the wound, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the bone is assembled in two parts, as there are two branches; then cover the other part as you have done the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put in the wound linen soaked in rose oil; and put on top of that other linen soaked in wine and oil, and place two poultices on top, and cover with doubled cloths, and tie it over all the limb according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and place them according to this resemblance and be assembled by sewing in the neck of the drawers, and one of the parts of the patient's back, and the other at the part of the little finger; and the other head above the two angles, and everything assembled is restricted in the loop of the drawer; and never is this branch of the cautery in the form of iron, and it is that you take one cauterizing needle, and cover the skin of the wounds, and be heated as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the poison is discovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that sap with a thin needle, and the skin with this subtle cautery clean:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the copper in all ways that you can, until you extract everything; and guard that the feet do not touch the wound; and make sure that this work is safer; and watch out for the flow of blood, and make sure that the work of tailoring does not make any harm, and make sure that nothing goes wrong, if something goes against you, whether an abscess or the flow of blood or other harmful thing, then cure what goes against you according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the pain is not severe, and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then use perforation, as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the sharp instrument is laid, then place the pain on the raised seat; then perforate the abscess in the part below all the spatula wide, and put the perforation down the long body; and let the wounds be wide so that all the sharp edge flows; then put cotton on the limb, and tie it, and let the remaining sharp edge flow, then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the sharp edge come out of the wound mouth, then you must go with a pen or the instrument that treats the sharp edges of dropsy, because its form is as before; and expand the wound, and make sure that the sharp edge returns, and is assembled after six months or around, and when it is assembled as before, and so the pain will pass its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the kidneys
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	in the section of this branch, there are many positions that cause fear in many people, so it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you about the work and similar things.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the backbone, and even from the kidneys; and it is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive sharp and cold, which is spread in the kidneys, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the blood; and it does not cause pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps some gray, putrid, and pus-filled abscesses, and of yellowish color, and sometimes comes from an outflow of arterial blood, or from an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the presence of a high abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their appearance with gentle touching of the fingers, and can often make a cut across this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you should carefully watch the circulation of blood, then stop the flow at the top, and pull out the thread from the white face, and deliver the suspended part of all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already soaked with these needles, then it should be cut and cleaned; and if it is in the face, or inside the vessels, then it should be delivered completely, and cleaned roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the shoulder blade is the part that has not yet grown, then you must cover it all, and extract the bone, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped by an envelope similar to a blister, with the softening of the groin, and the pain is severe when it moves; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and therefore we will tell you the work of treating this, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to seat the dislocated joint on its own, then lift the suspensory ligament of the tendons to your fingers, and all the tendons that are close to the bone, and tie them with the masters, and extend them evenly; then cut the spatula sharply across the middle of the tendons, as far as they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arrows which are in the temples; then take a needle or double thread, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came from, and tie it on the other end; then cut them diagonally, straight up, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as in the others, so that none of the tendons are torn; for by this no harm comes, and if all the tendons come out, it is necessary to pull the tendons from all the tendons; so that he does not lose his blood through the incision of the tendons, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the tooth
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are due to the section that comes from or by the tooth breaking, or the extension over the stomach in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that break to one of the joints; and this break is either from the tooth breaking, or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes are: from impact, or from jumping, or from screaming, or from lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs that indicate the extension of the tooth breaking, are that it happens little by little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal to the front, because the tooth approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the gum, which causes sudden pain at the beginning, and is different abscesses appearing outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart after the section of the gum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the entrails are torn with the intestines, and are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the injury, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with fear, because it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or fear that the intestine be wound around your hand inside the wound, if it can enter; then hold it between your hands and loosen the fingers; then place the skin above, and cover all the skin of the ribs with the long one that you have for opening the wound, as many as there are that come out; then remove the white skin that is outside the skin of the ribs, until the white skin does not show from all sides; then put your index finger in the direction that leads to the rib, between the white skin that is outside the skin of the ribs and between the second white skin, and behind the rib, and between the second white skin; and move gently with your right hand inside the skin of the ribs, and place the white skin high on your left hand, and loosen the skin over the abdomen; and command the servant to extend the skin upwards, and remove what is behind the bandage; and if you find anything, if you find any intestine or white skin, then put it in the belly outside; then take a needle or a thick thread made of 12 threads, and put it in the back part of the skin, which is after the skin of the ribs; then cover the threads with the skin, and form them into two layers, so that none of the vessels that they touch can enter, as the pus does not come out; and then place the first layer according to the first layer, and the two layers afterwards according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cover the part that is outside the skin of the ribs with the great one of a finger; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cover in the part that is outside the skin of the ribs, as we have said before; then apply soft linen oil to the wounds, and put it on the wound, and it will be applied to the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white pus that we have said after incision, due to fear of blood clotting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the wound bleed for itself; and if it takes a long time to stop, then sprinkle with hot vinegar, and put on what we have said, until it stops; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma

And the ancients said that it is made thus as the branch which is together with the viscera, in a way that you tie the vessels, after the belly slightly above the navel; then cover it, and treat the abscess with what works, until the vessels heal; and the treatment is as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.

Never come a tear or anger, as we have said, and open the wounds; and let no one draw out any of the intestines, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and in all ways, if it remains too long at this point, the patient believes that the pain or the intestine is coming out; and this happens by the extension of the intestine which is at the tear, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and inflated the wounds and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and no cure is done in this way: and it is that the hairs are gathered together on top of their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the tear enflated according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the intestine which is outside the skin that covers it, then take the right and put it on top of the wound of the tear; and press at the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds above the head of the right, and both; then pull out the head of the right, and do not cover the intestine or stretch the belly or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, remove the foreign matter and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The thread is strained, and does not appear to be broken, and the cauteries are quiet in this limb, and closer to recovery.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of leather of boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of boots is softened in some men, because the charcoal inside is softened, and it can be seen; and it is a matter when one wants to cure it, that one should make the wound lie flat on its back, and cut the leather that is softened over the natural leather; then bring the two edges together at a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess soft leather at three or four seams firmly; then stitch between the seams, and treat the wound as with other wounds until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	For gently
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	For gently is commended in our law, and because I would not speak of it in this book; and there are only two ways: one is that the patient should answer gently when asked, and be treated gently; and the other, because we often have need to use gentleness with some animals to help us, such as a goat and sheep and cat and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that gentleness is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the animal sit in high heat, until the sinews are softened and remain; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the chastening of the belly: it is necessary that you smear the beast with oil, and press the skin of the intestines with your right hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cope over each opening with a cloth, when you have well cauterized them; and leave no trace of the sharp and subtle thorn which is on the vessels; and this method of chastening is milder than that which is done by attraction, because by attraction something of the intestines may remain, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is in two ways according to men: one is that between the two testicles, open as wide as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has a penis like a finger and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is that you cover all the wounds and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Of the tendon
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tendon is a wound open on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you clean the excess of the tentigenous matter from your hand or fingers, and wipe it lightly; and do not move too much in front, because blood does not come, then cure other cures until they are healed; and to another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use, and perhaps it jumps out, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason they call the ancient "cowbird disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you wipe it as we have said about the tentigenous matter, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient that the error is when the woman's nature is not well perceived, or when the birth is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to her; or it is by charm awakened, or a subtle or sharp sorcery, and it is done in the marriage bed, or in the sides, or elsewhere; and they prevent conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the look of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close and near, it is either to you or to the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a delicate and subtle syphilitic ulcer, and it is near the two lips, then hurry, and do as follows: bring your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spread her legs; then form the two lips, until the subtle syphilitic ulcer is drawn out, and is over the stopper; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and put it on the ulcer, and cover the woman with a blanket each day, so that she cannot sleep.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the ulcer is hard and spongy, it is necessary to apply a poultice similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the limb is from a horse, if the bone is crushed and broken, and apply stanching medicines such as blood, dragon's blood, incense, and an abundance of wax; then apply a large piece of clean cloth, so that the wound does not stick; and thus it should be long, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a horse, if it needs to be covered, do so according to this manner, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without a cut usually do not close; and when hemorrhoids become old they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thromboses, when they are formed in the marshlands, and do not appear until sensed, can only be cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marshlands, which can be sensed, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the arm on tenterhooks, and cut the tendon at its root, then powder with medicines that stop bleeding, such as acid and blood of dragons and incense, and similar things; then let her soak her feet in cold water for an hour, then place her in very cold; if blood flows, sit her in a decoction of sumac and scarred pomegranate skins and galls and similar things, and then take flour of wheat, and mix with honey and oil, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he becomes weak, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without causing injury; then take the limb, and moisten it with plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and apply to the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, cure the limb with poultices until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles the sharp edge of a knife, if it should cover it as I have said the thelul; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess come from the marsh, such as chancre and pus-filled abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and pus-filled abscess chaut, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary to tell in this treatment about the abscess chaut that comes from the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that fill with pus; and if you know how to treat with iron, look at whether the abscess is agus at the beginning of its coming, and plain of cholor and fever, and if it becomes red see if you can treat it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but make the patient wait until the pain is alleviated; and then place the injured part on a chair, and have two small chairs where it leans, and rest it on its back and gather its feet to the sides of the leg; and let its knees be spread, and put its arms off its hips, and tie them firmly with a good bandage; then bring the splint against the right side, and let it be administered with the tool that opens the mouth of the wound, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this tool being administered, you check the depth of the wound, so that what enters into it does not go deeper than it should, and does not bruise the injured part; and if the tool is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with bandages, so that the tool does not hurt it; and it is necessary for him to put the horn of the tool on top, and to stain the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess is open and it is being squeezed by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with a sponge; and when the wound is drained, it is necessary to put moist lint in the wound with rose oil or dry vinegar; and place the bandage on the edge of the marsh, and place it above the marsh and above the other clean moist lint boiled in water or mustard seeds cooked; then after two hours of poulticing, until it is healed; and never lift the bandage and the wound with a poultice of boiled water and honey, and then with boiled water or roots of lis and aristolochia long cooked; then reapply the poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sewn up in the marsh, it is necessary to avoid cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman pressing down and wanting to smell the air: then hasten the baby to come out; therefore check that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the second born with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press on his belly, so that the baby comes out quickly; for when he comes down from his head, the second is with him, and is cleaned of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes out of its place, and comes forth from the back or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes up over the belly, or sometimes, and is turned over onto its own neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the dancer that she be wise and subtle in these things, and if she goes wrong from error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out of its head naturally, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a seat, or the women hold her; and rub her with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then give the dancer a small amount of the following form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second one, and apply pressure to its angle until the moisture that is inside has been removed; and take the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not, then it is necessary to cluster the woman with fenugreek powder mixed with mustard oil; then let her inhale and expel the condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now brings down the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, it is necessary to gently and gradually reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up; then remove the chair from the ground, and wash the woman, so that she does not faint at the removal; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then press the hands against the abdomen that was previously placed there, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it should be placed high up; then gradually turn it little by little, until it is level; then grasp both feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up after crying, command it to lie down and extend its neck; if it jumps up again, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not lie down as we have said, gradually turn it little by little, until it is in a natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be lying down.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take a mussel shell, and oil of sisamine, and melted lead, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until above the ribs; and when she is softened from above, make her a collar of mint, and put it on, and let it stay for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's knees over its hips
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place its hands gently and gently; then it should be held upright on its neck, and its legs hang down, and it lies on the bed; and gently fold its hands, and then grasp its hands above its stomach, and remove its clothes little by little, until it is cleaned from below; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and gently move its stomach upwards, then gently push your hands down; and slowly feed the child a little at a time; and command the woman to hold the child until it is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of a child who comes out with a wide hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman up and leave; if she cannot leave, lift her onto the bed and straighten her legs; then apply the muscle relaxation that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, sit her on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand; and when the child is born, shape it according to its natural figure, and make it sneeze, and command that it be pinched until the baby cries.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of a child on its back, and has spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I advise that the patient soak their hand in water, then turn it gently and lightly; when it is even, place on the muscle-like substance of olive oil and honey, as we have said, then command them to move it gently; when you have done this, seat it on a chair, and command them to sit; and spit out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all the other joints.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this for all the other joints, bend the joint to your elbow, until the moisture is drained; and if it can be bent over its face and neck, cover it with a cloth, so that it is not held back, and die the child; then push the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to sit once: then it becomes even.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the discharge of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Saied that twins are born many times, and sometimes not at all in their birth; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is a strange thing, and they do not live if they are not named; I know that they are multiplied, and they are separated by the umbilical cord which connects them, which is like a belt; and sometimes they come out naturally as one or two at a time, just like we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out harshly, as the care we have said, and if the afterbirth is subtle, and do it soon and lightly what it does; and do so that it is worth moving to save.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	There are no cases where they are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or even more than fifteen years old, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise one, and it is fitting that the baptizer should do everything, because perhaps similar things happen to him; if so, do according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you care for the woman of the dead child or belly, if as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manual work; if it is fitting that the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she fears death; then the woman should be laid on her back, and her legs raised; and the minister applies two fingers, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated by the expulsion of the child; then rub the mouth of the child with moistened oils and muskills of althea and fenugreek seed, and semen of linseed; then apply the hands of the midwife with these oils and muskills; then pour them lightly into the mouth, then give her a draught of whatever is suitable to her, and if the child appears to be expelled above his head; if it is not expelled, place the fingers in his eyes or on his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or behind the beard or in the forehead or at the sides of the chest, and if it is expelled, place the fingers on the sides of the middle;
