and it is fitting that the midwife ties the cord to her right hand, and places the forceps between her left hand, and pours all over her hand lightly, and apply the fingers in any of these ways until the thing comes out empty; and this is the form of the child:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then flip to another one, where the doctor has skill, so that the extraction is equal; and then place it equally by moving from one side to the other, to help it move, and keep the teeth together as before.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, use some of its own oil, and put it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if it does not remain, place this bone or higher up on the shoulder, and do this as much as it can come out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by pulling, then you must wrap it around the wound, until it is completely out; then cover it in the joint of the foot or at the heel, and so you must do in the other hand, and in both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child is large and stiff at the neck, or has a sharp knot, it is necessary to beat the spatulated bone between your fingers, and make the knot and straighten it; or you can break it with an instrument called «almidach», from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and thus also do for the child's head naturally; and then pull the bones with pliers, and if the child's neck is stiff and held, if it is cut, until the blood issues; and if it cannot issue, then cut it in pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to prick it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is hanging by its feet, then light traction is applied, and the marshmallow is gently placed in the mouth.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the child is stuck in the stomach or in the groin, it is advisable to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and after uncovering the stomach or groin, as long as the moisture that is there is removed. And if the other limbs are broken, and the child remains, then you should wipe the mouth with a marshmallow, and pull it to the mouth of the marshmallow; then wait one or two minutes, and pull it out. And if the mouth of the marshmallow is retracted due to an abscess that has formed there, it is not necessary to force it, but rather to administer moist and greasy things; and the ointments are applied, and the scar is treated with hot, softening and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the bone is above its shoulder, and you can put it back in place, as we have said for the living child; and if there is no way to do so, then treat it by breaking pieces, and leave nothing of the second joint.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, then put it in high restriction, and treat with other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted another doctor about it, and he also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the groin, and they grew so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not sew the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive, and it pulled out some bones, and after some time, others came out.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and there were many bones, so much that the woman was not in any better condition; and I saw the woman for a long time like this, and it was only a little blood from the wound; and I had not remembered this chapter before because when masters find an unusual thing, they do not know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marble back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and then comes the form of pressure, by which we apply books; and to return to the previous question of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the corners should be more subtle than the restraint, and made of flat or wooden material; and the mouth of the pipe should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half long; and in the two joints, they should be two stoppers of this same pipe, which should be firmly placed on both sides, half a palm or more long; and these two stoppers are inserted into the mouth of the marble when turning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of an ebony or boxwood rod, according to the appearance of needles; and it should have two prongs, as you see, about one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the wound all the way with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs apart, then push the two prongs into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument, as you would with needles, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the wound, until the bail does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surmounted by a handle, and they have many similarities; and when the one sees them matched, the more sharp the work, and the higher it is to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument because you have not matched it, for its need is not excuseable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is held to the childhood, it is necessary that you command the pain that it retains its saliva, and then make it spit out the condition, and hold your hands to the mouth and nose; and if it sneezes through this, well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make or prick holes in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, camomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or poultice of pot in the mouth of the marsh, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and let it steep until the vapors come into the mouth; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second attempt fails.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and is not much better, command the bath attendant to moisten her right hand with wheat oil or musk oil, and then put it in its natural position, and try the second attempt; and when she finds it, grasp it gently and extend it straight, so that the marsh does not crack during extraction; but move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull out; it will come out and dislodge.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the wound in the gum is narrow, we have said the cure of expectoration and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not all that we have said, then guard that you do not follow the advice; but it is better that what is at the wound in the gum, that you tie it to the cheek of the woman, then cleanse it with the ointment tetrafarmaçon; so it will heal and return, and be well. However, when it heals if there comes a bad smell to the stomach and head, and causes pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use fumigations such as: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cresses and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fume the woman during retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass-like appearance like a hook, and one places the head subtly in the fire, and the sparks are placed over the fire; and the fumigations are done on the charcoal, and the tine is used until it is burned out, and then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but it has been stupefied by some subtle syphilitic infection; therefore, one must then apply a blister to that spot, and do not pierce any more with the sharp instrument, and keep the bandage away from touching it; then place on the wound moistened with wine and oil, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, place or sprain a bandage on it, and let it rest for a while, and it should be stretched as the child wants to go into the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never come such swellings of wound infection or abscess; if cover the wound: if cured, as we have said of the bandage of bread.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the deep fistula foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodular, and thicker than those that come above the foundation, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and becomes moist with white or subtle pus, and never these fistulas persist; and they are known by the fact that there is outflow or ventosity when the pain makes an outflow, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate half of the urethra; and they reach the joint of the hip, and perforate out of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the base, and not passing: and it is that you should bore your second finger or base, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you insert a thin tent of cloth, or horsehair, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation, egestion, or ventosity, as we have said: cut so that it does not perforate more; then hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is located near the bladder or near a urinary tract, if it allows urine to pass through, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is located near the ribcage, then the tendon comes from the limb; if there is no twisting and the location of the pain is not clear, it is because it is inside, and there is no cure by medicine or cauterization; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure but labor and vanity of those who try.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pain is hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then drive a tent of tin, or lead if there is twisting, until you remove it.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your second finger, as if you are feeling for it; and if you sense between your thumb and index finger the swelling or the bone, then cut through it so that it is permanently healed; do not labor too much if it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can heal many things, but this is rare; and the aid that is done is that one heats the fine cauterizing tool according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and one puts it all through the fistula, until it reaches below the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred pieces are removed, which are similar to a splinter of wood; then the cure of moist wounds is applied, as long as those charred pieces are not removed, then the cure of ointment applying char and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If otherwise, nothing else can be healthy; and if it is between, and does not perforate just where it is based, and between your hand and the tent a thick covering of felt or syfac, and you see the fistula leading to the covering of the wound; if the copper at the beginning of the fistula, and before the tent, and then the cautery after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and it will be delivered from the tent, and closed; then clean those charred parts that seem like a quill of a goose, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot remove it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: it is to know, the burning of these arrows stuck, and the stopping of blood and the separation of moisture; then cure tents boiled in butter or crushed chocolate, until the wounds are poured out, and the arrows are removed from the wound; then cure the wound of the injuries soaked in strong charcoal, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from the base, it is distant from the body, and if you press on the top or base, and ask what it is.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the thread or the syringe or the charcoal, where it is close to piercing, if there are no other remedies except hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods: whether you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut just above the base, or if you can put tents and cure as in the first; and do not move too much in front, that you do not cover the part that holds the base, and the excretions come out through the sense of volition; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut below the base, or by a tent or other instrument appointed; then clean the char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to hold the fistula in the part before the base: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you push the tent into the fistula, it is often costive with the foundation below the skin above, so take a tent perforated at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the thread into the second, and push the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not found at the edge of the foundation within, then pull out the thread of that which is perforated, so that you push your second or foundation; and take the head of the thread, and bring together the two parts together, and hold one against the other, and let it remain for a day or two; and do not hold it again until the thread covers those that are between them and heal; then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then I will perforate it in all ways that you can, unless it is too painful.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make the application so painful if it is too painful, and then cure as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spongy tissue that is made into a fistula is very sharp and pointed on one side and cutting; and on the other part, not, because we do not want to cause more harm than necessary, as you see here.
des emorroydes	from the emerods
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in cutting them, blood flows; and there are many, and one or more, and they are under the fundament and at the top of the fundament. But those that are under have little moisture, and in cutting them, there is a little bit of sharp or yellow bile or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those within the fundament is that you command the patient to urinate through another chamber, until the fundament is cleansed, and the child appears; then you hasten, and grasp them with tweezers, or hold them at your finger, then cut them at their roots; and if the threads cannot hold them because of their moisture, you take them to a towel, or a cloth, or a piece of linen; and tie them in both hands, then grasp and powder with any hot powders that are in the cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the book of cautery, and cure them with other cures until they are healed. And if the fundament cannot come out, you apply a rough and sharp paste to clean what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out openly; then grasp them at your finger or with tweezers, and cut them, then cure as we have said until they are healed, and do not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to stitch the wound in this manner: take a thread of twisted hair, and make it into a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread away from the needle, and if it is too wide; and straighten the thread formally, then pull the thread, and pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put above the wound a piece of linen cloth soaked in rose oil or salve, and put above the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and firmly at the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occurs in the intestines due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is not helpful.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset the shoulder to the point of a spatula or at your angle, which does not allow moisture; then cure it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be cured, then begin the cutting more forcefully than before until it is healthy, and let it be scarred; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	dryly
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are a small appearance found in the chest, and it goes very deep; and sometimes they find the source, and one feels like a fever, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a needle of a goose feather, or a pen of a vulture very strong, and put that needle on the fever, until the circle around the fever encircles it completely; then turn your hand all around the needle until you cover it all, and push it deep, and extract the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if you make a needle of iron or steel in this form, and it is thin from below and thick above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	For the patient does not feel pain, to hold it at both ends, and press it; and if you see, then cauterize the heat, as it is before or in the chapter of the cauterizer.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cauterizer
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one has ever made a cauterizer of silver or bronze, or melted copper or wire; and no one has ever made any of these small and large instruments, according to those who will use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those that are used in the care of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small cauterizer is above wide, or the belly is tied as follows:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a disruption where the belly is tied, as you see, and the wound is in the middle perforated; and there are two perforations on one side and one on the other; and the belly or the person puts medicines in a beast's bladder or parchment, and there are small perforations all around, and there is a space of one finger between each perforation, then fill these perforations with a strong thread twisted into an X or spirally, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the wound is facing an instrument before a strong thread, then clutterize; and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or butter or something similar, then press it lightly; then the nurse gives the patient's two hands together, as much as possible, until it is all visible, then remove the poultice, and relieve the pain in his legs at once, and if the swelling wants to come out, if it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in a disease of diarrhea of the belly, and the patient wants to expel it, then restart it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if they are stuck at the base or in an abscess, then the poultice should be as delicate as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate poultice above where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We mentioned the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different depending on how they are made, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and for what reason they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by being pierced with a spear, and the cut of a sword or dagger, or lance or staff or siette, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as wounds that are made above the neck, or on the head, or on the foot, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds to the head, because its chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from a penetrating object or similar things, and if the skin is completely torn and is large, and you doubt lightly of abscess: if you do this soon, clean the wound itself immediately if there is little blood from the wound, and on the other hand, clean the part that is not affected; and avoid the evils of overeating and heavy food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to clean, let him eat light food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his diet; and put on the wound, if abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in sterile wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if his arm has been moved, put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot come together due to swelling, then sew them together, as I will say in wounds of the belly, by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and can be moved but only held by a small piece, then cover it with a bandage; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have a bruise or a piece of skin that is not attached to the bone, then cover it all with a bandage, and pour in warm water, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stanched by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you have a piece of skin that has come loose, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put this powder which boils as soon as the wound is moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is as follows: take a part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and the powder finely ground, and fill the wound, and hold it together until it sets well and joins all its edges; then bind it tightly, and leave it unloosened if it does not swell; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use chalk alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound is moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, immediately put this powder on it; but instead of any other ointment, use some made of flour of barley, with honey and water, until it heals; then treat with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about the main fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and the main fractures, but if the neck nerves or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other method than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, because it hurts bones and makes them retract; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and its continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member; but rather use gentle medicine, such as chalk washed in cold water, and mixed with rose oil, and the cloth washed in cold water, and other stones of this manner, and moist cloths.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then use bandages and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the bone is exposed and full of pus, then perforate or go deeper to the bone; if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then cauterize the wound, and bind it, and cauterize the wound as necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the muscles, and the conductor is preserved, by which the meat goes, if the cut is above the backbone of the neck, and do not touch the neck but return it according to its natural shape; then gradually tighten, and leave it for some time, then treat the wounds with ointments until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound is ready to close, and align the outlet; and if the wound is fresh, powder on top of the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then follow the treatment as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from an arrow or a dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from an arrow or a dagger, and the wound is deep, look to see if the hairs around the wound are standing up: cut them then, as the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh all over with blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood that it does not settle immediately, and return to the heart, and close the wound; but put attractive ointment on it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and make the wound sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor trembling of the heart from anything else; and when you see good dispositions, cut that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other injuries, as long as they are healing; and if they cannot heal, and work, then perform surgery to create a fistula; if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword cut, and it is simple, or more or less on the back, then cure it as it should be; if it is large, stitch it up; if it is small, apply powder, and if it has pierced bone and there are pieces, remove them if they are necessary; and if they are not necessary, let the wound rot, which will help with extraction; and for other wounds to other limbs, use judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. Belly rupture is great and medium and small; from the large wound, the intestines or the nerves of the intestines may escape, by which the infiltration of air occurs; and the wound is more painful, and the small wound is worse than the large one, because one should not put the intestines back without putting them back correctly; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, if they are put back incorrectly, and because the medium-sized wound is worse, because one must suture the intestines to their place as with other II And there are four ways in which the belly rupture occurs: the two common costures are in the belly wound, and the costure of the other wounds of the body and two other costures are common to other wounds; and all of them are more appropriate with the belly wound, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is injured, and it is easy to replace, it is done by one of the two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of dry hay, or cook it in hot water and wine and salt until the intestine swells; and never do this by force, and it is better to wait until it softens.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if the intestines are moist or wet and misshapen, because by this they are aligned and enter soon; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision with the instrument with which one removes tumors; and the first care is to stop the bleeding, as we should not cut without great necessity. And this is the instrument for cutting: slice from within the belly and outside, and remove the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, if you can put them back in their natural form according to their own place, it is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part away from the belly, it is necessary that you place the injured side on top of the patient's back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part away from the belly, then raise the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is appropriate, then insert a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leaving about an inch from the edge of the wound, and sew it with strong thread; then pierce the two layers of skin with the two needles, which are outside the skin, until you make a hole in that part, and bring the two needles together four times; then tie a double knot around the needle from both sides, then evenly sew the edges of the wound, leaving about an inch, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the whole wound, and thick ones cannot enter well: therefore, they should be medium-sized; and do not insert the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so that they do not cover and open the wound before sewing; then cover the edges of the needles, so that they do not stick to the injured part at night, and put bandages or cloths on the edges of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sealed; this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it can be done with one needle or two, the second stitching method is common, and it is that you bring together the edges of the skin and flesh and a needle with a strong thread; and when you have pierced these edges all together, then remove the needle from the part where you started, in the manner of sewing with a needle; and leave a space between each stitch the size of a small finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine as it had been for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with anything, as I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I put cotton soaked in honey over the wound twice a day, and washed it with vinegar until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle and the thread from one side to the other through the inside; when it has pierced the middle correctly, place the head of the suture or stitch where you have put the needle, and pierce it from the other side through the inside on the other side; and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier does the skins, and that you leave once the suture of one part, and repeat it on the other, until the whole sewing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the main threads to the other head, in this manner: stick a needle or thread near the wound, and make it pierce that part alone, and leave the two ends of the wound; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part inside, both ends of the wound, in two other threads that are on the other side. And this is the easiest method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says this word, and no one testifies to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each; and one needle must be inserted from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corroies; and that when the tear is in the belly, the sewing is more painful than other stitching of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you have probed the fresh wound to its full depth, and if the doctor has moved it, then remove the intestine and the lint; then put on powder infused with charcoal, and if the doctor has moved it, then apply any ointment present until the wound closes; then bind the cloth, and be careful of the sifac and the mirach; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to close, use cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For in many positions of the wounds, there is no other medicine besides simple ones; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light oil of temperate warmth, or rose oil, and put it around the wounds, and smear it on the bones; and if it feels pain or pruritus in the belly, and often happens, then clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the pruritus comes to the intestines; and pierce from within, and scrape what is inside, and what is inside the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines that are called "jeun" cannot be healed when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that are in them, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back in as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to black, then you must tie the black limb that is there, so that blood does not come out, for there are veins and arteries; then cover what is between the liver, and put the two needles hanging from the part outside the wound up to behind in order to align the extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, it can be restored to some men, because I saw that one man was gutted or stabbed in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an abscess and fistula, and inside there were excretions and ventositez; I made care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the legs sounded.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that the pains were not in his belly; but there was no pain, only it delayed in better dispositions, and drinking and eating; and some experienced people said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a way: take a hot iron, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the hot iron has opened the mouth, put it on top of the two lips, so that it holds its mouth above; then cover the wound, and hold it in such a way that it cannot slip, then put the other hot iron after in that manner before, until the wound is completely closed; and over the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the bone of the shoulder is broken inside the body, and no harm comes to the hairs, and it can be sewn with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of the intestinal thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thin thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and through the intestine, and sew it in the wound; and this way of sewing is not far from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the hollow intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except for its subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	that all wound or abscess, when it is covered, is universally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut and opened.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its hard and white tissue, where no pain is felt, and it is cut as thin as the quill of an eye; and sometimes it is clear and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, except for one of the EIGHT causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard pus inside, and on the lips, which does not allow new pus to be born; or there is too much pus; or the wounds are poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a form of plague; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and escapes by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas that is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or at the syphilitic sore, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in any of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are of great difficulty in healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the part I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, if the quill; and if the fistula is twisted, take a subtle tent of linen, for the linens do not stick to the twists; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well cover it with tents, cut it through one of the openings, for the moisture does not come from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then treat it properly to your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is well fastened in place, and ask well of the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, cut according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply placed in the right place, it is necessary to cut as much as you can, then put soft tents in medicine ague, and pour them in at the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous part that remains at the bottom; and then put clean ointments on the wound, as long as it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves cause pain or damage to the main limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove all the corruption until it is completely removed, then treat the things that have been injured with charms for as long as they are healthy; and if they are not healthy, and remain in the same way as before, then do not go further: if it is exposed and wants to be taken out as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too far in, and you cannot reach it; if there is no other method that is less painful to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with forceps, if it is extracted with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, and do not leave even one; and if the moisture makes it against you, and there is no error or fear, if you copper and moisture and charm, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them within an hour, place something soothing on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is completely rotten around the bones, and then they will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, raise the dead flesh as far as possible until the entire bone is exposed, then cover the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption remaining, and comes close to the bone; if it does, cover it completely with the corruption, and treat it as best you can until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
