Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matters came to the leg, and he was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no cause to open; but the midwife by their folly opened too high that the abscess opened, and they poured out much matter, and became a fistula, and there came much pus from the body; and many more sought cure within two years, and there was no healing in the art of hands, so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was coming out through the openings was great pain to the young man's body; and his body became red from the young man's age, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these gaps, and then I searched all the gaps, and found that one was coming against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the gaps until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from within; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with various remedies for a long time, but could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm of the bone, and treat it all over its length, then I treated it with remedies; and it became healthy and healed quickly, but it did not want to continue the work except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because often for the evacuation of blood, but he was completely healed, and born in the place of the bone a hard horn, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither to the former nor to the latter.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a thin strip of cloth, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended upwards; and put another thicker strip of cloth than the first strip, on top of the horn that is above the bone, and extend the head, so that you remove the rotten horn from the outside, and uncover the horn above the place where you see that it should be, so that it does not corrode the horn; and put a bandage or a cloth outside the bone to cover the rotten horn; and it should be done in such a way that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotted and does not open, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, then remove the entire crown; then apply the wax to the other part, and slowly fill the corruption from one part to the other, as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, then cover the corrupted joint, and sew the bone or it contains on the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way than to cover; and if the decay is at the tip of the hand or the tip of the foot, then this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you must ask about that corrosion, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve make you contrary; and know that the tools for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason you must prepare each similar work with its appropriate tool; and know that the work will show you the tool that you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have to use according to what it should be.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The patient's member will rot either because of a pus or because of a lack; and when you have medicine for that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then you must cover that member until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the pain escapes from death, or from malice, which is greater, from the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and becomes darker afterwards, as those corrosions spread from member to member, and take hold of the whole body; if you delay covering, and if it is because of the sting of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions and vipers and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the penis, then cover it, and do not give him any space to come near his hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes from the hand, if the bandage is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the bandage is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its power; and thus do what you can when the corrosion comes or pain: if it comes in the first joint, if the bandage after the other joint; and if it comes to the pain, if the bandage all the pain; and if it goes up the leg, if the bandage at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than that the limb dies; and the way of the bandage or the cloth the member is such that you tie it above and below, and extend some ministers one of the limbs below, and some ministers the other limb above, and uncover the bone that is between the two limbs to the width of a span, until the bone is exposed; then the bandage or cloth, and put on each part of the linen, so that the member does not touch the healthy skin, and brings the pain and abscess to the other.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flows when you are working, cauterize the limb hastily, or place some powders that stop bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a clean bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in such a case: he had a black wound that seemed like fire burning, and that corrosion first appeared on his face, taking over the whole face; and when the honorable man saw the corrosion, he covered the wound, and was healed; and after a while, the corrosion appeared again on his hand, and it came to me, and I placed some repercussive things after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I would cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he lost all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have not told you anything else except for what is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes an abscess in a lean body, and it lingers so long that it causes great swelling; then they burst and pierce, and the pus escapes, as if it were a bag; and the skin above is also thin like cloth, and does not stick to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus," and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the outside, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you must cut around it, and especially when it is thin, like cloth; and it does not heal for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the skin becomes hard and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin is charred, then use this ointment: look to see if the breasts are large, and the nipples smell badly, then use Egyptian medicine made as follows: take aloe, oil, and litargyr, equally, and put it in a bowl to boil in hot water until the medicine becomes red and has the same thickness as honey; then take as much as you need, and make it into a thick paste and thin paste, and apply the ointment to the breasts, and hold the nipple; leave the ointment on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breasts are clean and dry; and once a day, if there is no Egyptian medicine present, and you should take ashes of grapevine, and pour hot water over it, then let it cool, and apply the ointment, until you see that the breasts are clean; and if the pain cannot bear it, and the Egyptian medicine and the ash of grapevine do not help, then use an ointment of honey and melted wine, which has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the flesh ache; and when you have done this, and you see that the breasts are clean, then use an ointment made of rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments, as I have mentioned their properties in treating wounds; and if the nipple is too small, and the clister cannot enter, then enlarge it with a sharp instrument, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is large enough; and if the wound is too large, then cover it with a cloth or bandage, wherever the clister or the breast can enter, and if the discharge from the nipple is on top, then put the bandage on the bottom.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the shoulder is dislocated, do not let it hang; and if you cannot cover the back as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the shoulder moves to the lowest part where it is, for when the shoulder is dislocated, do not let it hang, and if you cannot cover the back as you see fit, arrange it in this manner: the shoulder should move smoothly downwards, and leave nothing of the shoulder; and take consolidative medicines to put on the back, and place a linen cloth over all the back; then cover the forces at the place of the swelling slightly larger than the first, for they are tightly bound with another cloth according to the size of the swelling, and place it on the swelling to straighten the shoulder, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and the one who is on the swelling often removes to straighten the shoulder, and wipe away whatever comes from the swelling, whether it is poison or a little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that moves over the swelling, then wipe away that the shoulder is already healed, and approach the health; and then remove the bandage in the morning, or the next day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is turned awkwardly after many hours, cut it out so that the breast does not become misshapen.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after a long time, do not despair of the health, for the health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take long to heal from wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if the breast is turned awkwardly after many hours, cut it out so that the breast does not become misshapen; and if the breast delays in becoming whole, and is distant, then apply moist substances and dry remedies, such as oil of roses, and the same remedy behind the medicine; take oil of roses, and mix it with old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and the same thing is done with honey when it becomes thick, when there is no oil of roses present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and make powder on the fire; and put it on a cloth, and place it on the breast, and never administer long pepper and celestial lily root, which is also like flour of wheat and centaury; and use simple or composite remedies: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long and not cured by this cure, then cut out the corruption, and make an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs; if the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from a small pocket of the hand, or foot, or by chance in other places; and when it is drained, and one does not take care, if the abscess comes back, and corrodes and flows so much that it reaches the root of the finger, and perhaps entirely corrodes it; and then there are corrosions up to the bone, as long as there is painful putrefaction, and the affected part is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help much, then it is necessary that you cut off all the remaining superfluous part of the finger, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bones are healthy and the joint is sound; and if the joint is close to the skin, and begins to prick, and the wound, then it is necessary to remove the skin from the joint that does not pierce the skin, and put it above, and cover this joint subtly and gently, and put above the remaining skin burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then care for the openings until they are healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it and drain it, because as much as the bone rots, it cannot heal; and if you see the other rotting, then cover it with a layer of soft material as described above, and care for it until it is healed; and if it is fierce, and swollen, and it causes great pain, then it must be healed first; then cover the joint with a thin layer of soft material by cutting across it, and make sure that the cut does not reach the skin that is outside the joint, because the hairs would cause too much pain; and if it does, then put something on top to relieve.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand should be sharp
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Those who are born with some men's hands should be all crooked, and perhaps they have bones or perhaps they have a thorn, and sometimes they have an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in none of the fingers do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger, perhaps they move; the length of the crooked one is light, in this way: cut it from its root with a wide sawmill.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you have the copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be in the back, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh around the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The similar things that come together at once come from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the wound that needs to be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths with rose oil, so that it does not scar; or you put between two pieces of thin leather, until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When it comes to both of its ends with the palm, it should be held as it should be.
des vils	of the evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large and swollen, filled with excessive melancholy, which comes in many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never give them any clyster of chalk, and then the healthy one from the basilisk.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is according to the two methods: one is that you hold it and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this way: first, the first leg of high hot water very strong, until the big without being subtly subdued, then strain the leg with the bad from above the knee to the part below the groin; then cut the vein in the thigh, or in II or III, a wide tail, then relieve and pull out the black blood from your hand, from one to the other, until as much blood can be suffered as the virtues of the bad can bear; then tie it, and command that he be stained with meat boiled with black herbs; and repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat and no longer hurt.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the leg according to this method: if there is much hair, shave the leg with the bad injury, then put it in hot water or bathe it, and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swells the veins; if you do not have hot water, heat it over the fire, and then apply a poultice of warm cloth to the wound, or on the part below the knee; then cover the skin with grease at the edge of the wound, and scrape the skin from every part until it appears when touched; it appears red and black, and looks like a white cord; then boil out the blood until it is clear of the skin, and then bandage it lightly to the edge of the wound, then apply another poultice for three days; then scrape the skin over the wound again until it appears, then lift it to the elbow, if you have the skill, and lift it to another joint, as you did before; then apply another bandage, or more if you have the skill, then lift it, and apply to the second joint, then draw and lift to the next joint; then draw and lift until the whole is free, then bandage; and if you cannot draw and lift, use a needle and thread to pull out the blood from the wound, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as long as there is any; be careful that it does not stick, for if it sticks, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it will do harm to the injury; and when you have treated the whole, place on the wound a linen cloth moistened in wine and rose oil; and treat until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the vision is blurred and twisted and surrounded together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must torture it but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron used to cover the eye is curved and does not cut into the vein; it has a large curve, because if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise in other parts than the legs, and if it comes out of the skin, as it does from within the body serpentine and winding, it should be tapped between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are such that it comes in the leg a very large inflammation, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And if the wound is open, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to two inches wide, and the wool, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not there, if the wrapping is around the cloth, and the wool; and if it is too long, cut a part, and wrap the remaining, and do not cover it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it will go back into the body, and bring abscess and pus to the limb, and bad sickness; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little from the top, and nothing remains or rots; and this wound never occurs when it is treated with one or ten palms of length, and sometimes I have seen it heal in a few days, as it was ten palms long, and when you cover it, if the pus bursts or perforates, and goes to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and let the matter inside be drained, and administer medicines for pus every day, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein, and even when it opens into the joint of the foot, or the toe, and there is much pain, and it suddenly stops; therefore, as we have said before, do this.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	birds that hatch between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that hatches between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, sensing well in member to member, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by the corruption of some humors, such as worms and lumbrics and ascarides or intestines; and one doubts its evil, for as it goes through the body, and it goes to the head, and it comes to the oil, perhaps it enters, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that the patient is being cured and drawn, it cannot be done otherwise than when he goes: therefore, you must lie the limb above and away from a very tightly bound strong bandage, then cut through and remove it, and if the blood comes out in front of the char, and you do not true it, then cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, then hold it away from it firmly, then cut through and remove it; and it is necessary to use the bandage of healing for the bodies of medicines soluble for the bad humors for the diseases.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered that one of her arms was swollen, and I saw a small abscess in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise as if a worm were at the shoulder, much faster than anything, just like live silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain departed from that arm, and went to the shoulder, and then shortly afterwards it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she had turned inside out around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I greatly marveled at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had often wanted to see how it moved from one limb to another, but I had not seen it in this way before; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry skin, and her veins exposed, and because that appearance of constraint appeared; and it did not appear in this way to those who were delicate, and who had moist skins and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it appears as we have described, lift the limb up and down quickly, and then press on it so that that constraint of the vein is removed; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat the cause of the veins, such as fetid pills, and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their similarities and according to the types of bodies they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are arrows with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and blunt; and those with two angles, and those with long necks, and those with pieces; and those that pierce any member however they may: or in a principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, is apparent: then it is necessary to extract this arrow, for many die afterwards; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not fully embedded, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and perforates the bone, and the eyebrow that is above the head, are blurred vision and dizziness and vertigo and vomiting and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it is without force from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps it is impaired speech and voice; and the white discharge from the wound resembles pus, and also like boiling water, and if this sign appears to you, then hold the arrow if it has not already come out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a dislocated shoulder when it falls or breaks, are that it is near the right breast, and feels like it was stuck in something hard, not moving; and by chance the shoulder moves like a chicken, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that a wound will not heal is that without any scab forming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the limbs change color, and the patient breathes high and seeks the cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead enters into the covering of the poor, it is beneath the small ribs; and it pours out much blood and great pain and gasping; and they move all the member of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead enters into the stomach, by chance if it jumps out of the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead enters into the belly, and it does not jump out of the wound through the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead enters into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes out after, and the pain is very great: it is certain that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and back and spine and hips and knees, and similar limbs, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that went through the arm into the root of the nose: I tried it, and took it out from the other side of the ear fat, and he was healed without any problem.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a case of an arrow that pierced through the oil paper and into the fat, and the arrow was returned, and it could only reach the tip towards the fist, and the arrow was large like a Turkish arrow, all iron without ears; the wound was healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And in a case of an arrow that pierced through the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and subtly removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And in a case of an arrow that pierced through a man, whether it was in the neck or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days without changing his condition; I cut into the wound, and pulled out, and removed it, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to heal a man who has an arrow shot out or fell on his back, and the wound was dressed over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man, who had an arrow shot into his face, and the wound was dressed over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was shot into the man of the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded for three days after it was shot.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a thin probe, and did not feel anything; but he felt pain and pricking on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow; I put a warm poultice on his head because the wounds did not enlarge; and it appeared to me that the wounds were from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed immediately, and the pain lasted a long time until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed medicine on the wound, which was open, and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead at the shoulder; then I poured in more medicine into the wound opening, until the point of the arrow became visible; and it passed through the end of four months, and then it began to rot; since I had pierced the wound with the tongs, and on one side and the other, and could not remove it; therefore, I continued to devise and engineer various instruments, until I found tongs made well, according to how its form will appear at the end of this chapter, so that I could extract it, and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the healers judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was healed by the wound, and the pain was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you may put your care on what I do not say, for the books cannot grasp everything; but the wise masters know well many things, and on what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instrument, in the removal of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs except in two ways: either by the way they enter, or from another part; and the one that comes out by the way it enters is an arrow entering into its own charnas, and has never come out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, let her stay until the charcoal is ready around her, and until the issue is alleviated; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot get out, let her stay thus for several days, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, then pierce all around with a subtle fore, until the bones around are expanded, and then draw it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but let her stay until it is even after several days, for if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrowhead is not stuck in the bone only, and does not come out by itself, and remains lodged for some time without causing harm, then do not try to remove it with force.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, then administer tar as I have told you; then treat the limb until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrowhead is hidden in the flesh so that it cannot be seen, then treat the entire wound with tar; and if you feel it, remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrowhead, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then leave it until the wound is healed; and remove the arrowhead if you can, and if it has ears attached to it that hold it in place, then carefully cut off the part that is stuck deeply into the flesh, and then break or pry open the ears of the arrowhead, until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrowhead while removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, place the arm around the shoulder until it is full, then pull it, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the vein makes it difficult, follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and guard against incising the nerve and the vein, and move as you can draw the arrow out without danger, or quickly, or tightly, or firmly; and place the wound according to the form it was in when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then place it according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that one can see or feel apparantly: cut then above, as much as the tongs can take, and then extract it: if it breaks now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, enlarging the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if there is arrow in the bone, and you see that it is pointed, and you administer it slightly, if you administer the instrument with the point of the arrow entering the hair of the instrument; and then push further, and if the arrow is caught, pull the instrument inwards to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is stuck, it is necessary to cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is in the neck or chest or abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it, if you can; do not cover the vein and nerve, then remove it, and then cut into the wound, if necessary; and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the arrows used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do it: big, medium, and small, according to the amount of blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle is like the beak of a bird, to point at the tip of the arrow, as in this way:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the hooks for putting and for holding is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins of the common body, of which there are XVI heads, that is to say: two "herbech" veins that are behind the ears; and the two arteries that are in the temples apparent; and two veins that are in the arm pits of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the front; and the vein that is at the chief of the nose; and the two jugulars that are on the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the two veins outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are five in each arm: the one is to the cephalic, and is on the right side, and is called "the main vein" by the people; and the middle is called "the forearm vein", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and is called "the vein of the chest" by the people; and the basilic is on the left side, and is called "the belly vein", and is above the fossa, and is the one that is opened, which opens manifestly above the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the auricular and the anular, and it is on the right arm; and in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: the one is outside the corbeure of the groin of the right side costeit, and the second sophene which is at the knee of the left side costeit; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the knee of the other costei; and in the other leg are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	For the dislocation of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good to sprinkle with old grain, and salt, and olive oil accustomed to them; and the quality of the saineir is as I said: and it is that the hairs strangely strain their neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and it feels the pain of the throat from both sides, and then signs of inflammation; then lift the curtain over the vein at the top of your index finger, and remove the lancet from there, and lift the vein up high, and cover it, as you have done in the other two veins, and correct the blood according to your necessity; then remove the inflammation, and place your index finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their covering and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The cautery of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the cautery of the cephalic diseases of the face, headache, and migraine; and the quality of the disease is such that the pain is strongest when the vein is twisted until it appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has the following form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the vein from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again of a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not necessary for the flames to be too hot; and the direction of the incision should be across, because the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flames when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The incision of the second veins that are in the two armpits helps with the elbow, and the wrist, and the forearm, and the palm, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their incision is such that the pain is strained by turning any limb, as before; then the incision, and let the incision be across, a little long with the flame, a little wide, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, perhaps it will break; then apply cloth to the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie it with thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose is good for ague, and for fevers, and for diseases of the face, such as headaches and fainting that comes in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the vein is such that the pains strengthen their neck, then strain their nose to your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on their lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well by itself, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not move too much at first, and apply cloth to the blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, for it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	For the treatment of the two jaws, it helps to narrow the alveoli, and at the beginning of meseling, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for eczema; and the quality of the treatment is that the pains are strangely removed from one and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pain, and the pains sit on the first seat, then clean the vein long with a little bit widely, then draw the blood tempremently, or as much as the matter is; then do another part in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and hold the veins steadily, that the pains do not strangle; and leave it just before morning, that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the livers above the teeth helps in chewing in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and bad breath and around
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the pain disappear in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore match both, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, match the largest of each part, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disorder
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The disorder of the veins that are outside the tongue is helpful after the disorder of the cephalic, and it is the tightness of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the saintifier is that the maladies cease between your hands before the sun, and the lieve the tongue, and look outside each side one black vein: therefore heal both, and do not move too much, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the ear that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pricking at all times with a wide, sharp flame, or with a thin needle like a trephine, and is called "aneurysm"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire mirror is very famous, and it is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the task of opening veins that are deeply and clearly visible, containing large amounts of blood and turbidity; and this is the form of the fire mirror.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicate in its application, and it is for purifying fine veins, where there is fine blood; and this is the form of the fire mirror.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The purification of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the shoulder, and where the stomach; and it is necessary for the purifier to purge it well, and to remove the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then it should be stanched, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with fire, but cut off as we do with arrows.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, then it should be pricked and changed to another; or you want any rain of blood, or you save in place of blood the blood in the arm: it opens clearly; and it is pierced with fire as we have said.
