Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the place of the vein, then it should also be pricked and the arm moved until you touch the vein; then sign the vein of the entrance, and then bind the arm, and pierce the vein with fire as we have said; and beware that you do not prick in the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood gushing out as high as a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, it is from an artery: act quickly then, place your hand longwise, then press on the wound without stopping, which often happens; hold the arm still, and let the bad move not; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stopped, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, if you can, close the artery if it is open, because the main part of the blood flows out; stop the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take an escharotic of figs, and make it into a paste, and take one of the halves and apply it to the other side well; if it is without pus, it is good; if not, if the cure, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stoppings are not greasy in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the little arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The purging of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood from above, and from the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the purger should move all the veins that are out of place, and if he does not find them too painful, and he finds the vein, and he inflates it, and the salve is greasy, and sometimes cannot heal; and this vein opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you should use the purger with a needle; and shield the vein from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If it has veins between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein is helpful, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes; and it should be bled by pricking at the olive oil or mustard, for this is the safest of all veins, as it does not contain any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to seek the lightest vein, and not cause any harm if one must do it for the first time, and then restart; and by chance, some men's veins swell at first, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about health is that health is maintained only to maintain health and to prevent diseases from coming; and it should be done in one of the three ways that are either costly: namely, cephalic, fasting, and basilic; and if you should heal at the beginning of praying at dawn, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and if you should heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine that is administered for diseases does not have a determined hour or time, but rather as needed, in all hours and in all times; and it does not matter to sain the children until the age of fourteen years, nor the woman carrying except for the first four months up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Neither should one administer medicine to the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wants to medicate, in any way that it is, one must first clean the intestines of a light clyster, if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract excess and harmful intestinal matter to the principal limbs; and one should not medicate those who are too fond of meats, or those who are full, as much as they can be, nor hydropics; and if one wants to medicate after colic passion, vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent habitation at a woman, and pregnancy, and watchfulness and fasting, and that all the virtue, or by some thing of the arm or body; then subtly the humors, if one has the power, by foods and drinks and medicines, if one has them; then between or bath, if nothing prevents, to subtilize the blood, and to medicate from the vein the worst time around the third, as we have said; and to guard that day of work, and of pain, and of luxury, and of similar things; and to be tied and joined, and to be the medicator higher than that one who is medicated, and the flesh of the arm rub twice or three times, then raise the joint slightly with movement, because when it is too stiff or little, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the medication on the hand until the veins swell, and the one feels on; then moisten the medication with a drop of old oil, then put its dose on its right hand over the vein of the hand wherever it wants to medicate, that the vein does not burst and fail to hit.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as if they were strings at the incision, and some that are plain of their softness, such that when one puts above the flame, they draw back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if they open the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it must be that the surgeon is aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then one should try again a little below that place or above, until the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the hairs spread out, then leave it for one or two days, and do not tie the arm: perhaps an abscess will come; do not enter or bathe, then restart the incision if it pleases; and if the wound is small, or the skin is cut subtly and you doubt that there will be as much blood as you saw, then trust in that wound itself to the flame directly; and work a little gently, also when the veins are inflamed.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swelling, do not immediately restart the bleeding, and place a small amount of oil on it, as it soothes the course of the blood, and is quiet in this limb, like the oil; and thus administer the oil in every wound that you cleanse, to stop the flow of the blood; and the same thing applies to a plaster and bandage, when it is placed on the limb; if it is too thick, gently remove the blood and separate it.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess that often happens, exactly when it is not cleaned except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and place on the limb a soft sponge in hot water and a cloth a little thick, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any days without any blackness or greenness, then do not remove it; and if you see, place on it anything of aloes or of myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the wound to the soundness of the church: place your hand on it, and if you feel the swelling heavily under the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not place anything that we have said on it, because perhaps you will cut the artery; but apply a dry bandage to harden the wound, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it swollen, let it bleed until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is weak and outside, and has a job of arrow extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let him rest often and little, and let him be bandaged diagonally, not by pinching; and this way of bandaging is safe from the detachment of arrows and the compression of nerves, and it is better than the bandaging that is long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body is weak at the time of bandaging, it is appropriate to give them moist bread in apple cider; if they are hot, take out the arrow three or four times and apply the bread; and if they are cold in constitution, before the bandaging give them moist bread in honey mustard, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he palms the wound after much bleeding, it is necessary that he take a broth of charcoal and an odorous syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bandage an arm, and bleed again, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bleeding, he bandages a little and little, according to the amount of its continuity.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bandage an arm after the first bleeding, and he has a great deal of pain, he should bandage seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And those who wish to heal on the other side, they must heal at the second hour or at the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already hot, and causes fever; if they must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bursts; then one must wait for all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand upon the wound as it heals, so that the patient does not die from the bursting; and this has happened many times when the healer is negligent; and one should not do this unless one sees the arm coming out of the vein, and draw blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that one press firmly upon it; or if it is curved, extend the arm forcefully, for this would be harmful; but let it remain as it heals the second time; or until the frozen sinew from the vein has melted, and place a small amount of salt on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if it is swollen, let it be and do not press it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood the second time, let it be drawn from that limb itself, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy instead of the main one because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of this drawing is that the vein bubbles its hand in hot water, until the blood is red; then tie it gently, so that the vein appears well, then draw blood through the middle, not too narrow or too long; and let the punctures be wide, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow in the hot, until you have enough; and if it is still there, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it puts more in than it was; and this drawing from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the sainie of the hand of the right side is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the blood is drawn out, if one can see it; and if the salve goes against, and if you apply it with everything together, it will not hurt anything; and do not move it too much, for the nerves are all exposed to the bone, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary for you, put oil and silk on the wound to sew quickly, and do this for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the hand on the right side is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the soap plant is good for all diseases that are not in the body, such as marsh diseases, and retention of flowers, and rain disease, and diseases of the cocks and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that diseases bloat up in sharp hot water, and rub on the vein until it perishes, and bind above the joint of the bone; and the vein is at the knee, and through the bone many rains go; therefore the salve there or larger rain, or at the knee, is very good.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have the healthy ones above your belly, and you are surrounded by those who are dislocated, and the healthy one crosses as in copulating; and let the flames be equal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get out of the sickbed, put the belly in the high place, and let the vein well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healthy one needs to be the first time, then start the second above a little, because the veins are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the same sophene of the other belly equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the elbow is at the wrist, and its healthy one is worth the pain of the back, when it is for an abscess.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sweat is such that the hairs between or in the bath, and it is strange above the ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is better to cover it, for the legs are clean, and it is very prone to people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not straighten it, then it heals no pain from those who open or close the door, and towards the small toe, and guards against the nerves; and correct so much blood that you see, and then remove the ligament, and put it on cotton and keep it steady; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of sores by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either all at once, or gradually; and suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, with some being all over the chest; and the others are moved to the neck; and the other two are on the sides of the neck; and the suction below the chin; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the knees; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction on the heels; and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with drawing blood; and it should not be administered, neither at all heat nor without heat, in any disease caused by repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessary for diseases, one must ventilate, or by habit, one should ventilate every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each ten; for there are such who, when they have the need to ventilate, have heavy breathing; and some who feel repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at their neck, and in their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and taste it, and spit it out; and some who sing, and see through blood and tears, and die and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sweating of the head helps to cure the headache … that comes from the eyes, and should only be done after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in place of the sweating of the cephalic, and should only be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, for this does great harm; and for this reason it should not be used by those who are guards or who have other cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover, if they become forgetful, and for this reason, it is necessary to place the bandage a little lower due to the uncertainty of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The bandage around the neck is in the place of the neck and the collarbone, and for this reason, it is necessary to tighten it at the narrowest point, and to press against the windpipe, and to all, and to repetition; and it should be placed a little loosely, because if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach pain and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The bandage around the two ribs of the collarbone is necessary for headaches, and obtunding, and emigraines, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healing of the collarbone; and it is necessary to command the patient to place their hand when applying, that they do not press against the artery, and do not cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilation of the face is beneficial for mouth diseases, and corruption of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that come from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation of the elbows is as beneficial as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and commands the sick one not to move too much in front, for the inside is bare of flesh, and knows how to draw out nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the back should be used for emollients from the foundation, and for diseases of the soles, and it should be a large one made of metal, which must be able to pull well; and by chance, if it is too thin, it will break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups open widely, as they attract blood from the whole body, and are useful for ancient pains of the rain, of the marsh, and of the bladder, and remove the fleas; and they are in the place of the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and bring on pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is that you first apply it empty and quickly suck, then press firmly and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the flesh red and swollen, and reveal the blood vessel; then stop, and replace the cups, and take care of the body's position, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: if it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood;
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very sharp, you must strike it three times; and when we want to pull out the arrow slowly and slowly, we should only hit it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to get a lot of blood, we should often strike; and if the bone is sharp, we should strike it in front, and the end should be that the wound is perceived softly, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are hard, and who have stones, that you use the points of the oil vapors appetizing and dissolving: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal, or of lily, or of camomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of tarr, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom one wants to bind a wide and loose bandage, one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after ventilation with hot rose water, or hot cold water, or hot marjoram water, or hot cucumber water, or hot porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they are raised with vinegar, or hot water of mint, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive swelling rise from old wine, or vinegar of the sick, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be bled before or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep afterwards, and it is good that they move around when they should be bled and when they are being bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are bled are feverish, and if they are not too weak and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as large apples and endives and lettuces in milk, and similar things; and they should drink puce juice, and char of Castleton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	For those who have a cold constitution, take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little juice, and a little pulp and small nuts and pigeons; and the day they will vomit, they should drink more than usual; and it is appropriate to give some myrtle or muscat grapes before or after vomiting, to strengthen the main members; but it should not be given to everyone, only those who are very cold.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the sciatica, and on the stomach and the buttocks and the legs and the hip, for these members do not bear pain on their surface, and only one is done to draw blood from member to member, as we put suction cups on the breast when the baby is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and the buttocks to soften the member; and to relieve pain, when there is an abscess or stone, if by its attractive power it happens to draw out the abscess, or remove the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for their own sake alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with hot steam, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot steam or hot water where he has cooked harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction applied by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two large and half-palm-wide openings and a small opening in the middle, like to put a needle, and it should be made of tin, and soft leather before putting it on the limb; and it should have a thin rod of tin or iron in the middle to put a cord, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suctions of children are different from those of the old, and the thin ones are different from the thick.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction cup on the limb: take the candle of wax or the liniment, and put it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the hair; and then place it on the limb, and one should do so as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes, and remove the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and repeat often, if you have business.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore that is used in the disease of pleurisy, at all sharp, does not have a rod or a stopper, and is not administered except when it is full of sharp, and is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	No sutures are used except in members where one cannot apply adhesives due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in similar parts, such as ears or nostrils, and others similar; and the quality of using them is that when you remove sutures that are in soft wounds without causing pus, take them; and put them in a soft wound, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse the wound and the sutures, then rub the member until it is red, and put the sutures on the wound; and when they are smooth and healed, if it is a part where one can apply adhesives, apply them, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb from below, and then from above, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the running of the pus, soak a cloth in cold linen, and put it on, until the wound is cleansed; and if the wound multiplies, put on shredded gauze, or bandages, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you put half of pounded flour on the wound, and let it sit until it dries to the limb, it will stop now; and if you have more, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the snakes do not want to take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you make a needle so that the snake bites it, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they die; and when you see that they are dying, powder with a little aloe and crushed silk, or ash, if they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear child, that the foolish man who has never seen any of the old books, nor read any letter; and for this reason the science is unknown in our land, because I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the language and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twist or wound comes to any part, it is necessary that you hasten to clean the wound on both sides, if nothing happens, such as weakening of the body, or children, or elderly; or if the pain is not too great, or too sharp; and use sharp remedies, that is to say, sharp joints, and eye and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and use no heavy meats, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; then the pains return to their former government as they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a thick poultice of meat that makes large norrissement, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and ris, and tests, and pies, and flitches of veal, and oysters, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the poultice should be changed frequently and sooner than the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And be aware that the broken bones of old people and the decrepit do not heal well or heal together according to their nature due to the scarring of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, reset the broken bone above the joint, and join the member together, as it was before; and do not leave it for a long time without its work, and for this reason, it is necessary to apply thick meat poultices, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are various ways of breaking bones in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	Because the breaking of the shoulder is different from the breaking of the leg or arm, and I will tell you all the ways of breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a break that goes through the elbow, and another in water, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own method, and its proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and the break of the bone is known by the bone being twisted, and open wide from the deficiency, and it is at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or it is not at the touch, and the pains are not great, if there is no break; but it can still have twisting, or a cut, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but place the medicines that come after this, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the broken part that was in a whirlwind, and the two parts are disjointed, you must now put them evenly, as if they were inflamed; and if they are inflamed and come, let it not have any joint, until the inflammation is calmed; then place it evenly to the muscle that you can lightly and safely, and if it is restored, it is lighter than the restorations of this or he has pieces; then hold it, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if it is in a broken bone at the foot, if it is in two pieces, whether by hand or by string, or by your hand if it is small members, or by two strings, or by one string and by your hand; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are joined together, you should gently move them according to what you can, and guard that by your work no harmful injury or pain comes; and well join the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if it feels good to the touch, if you think it is not quite right: then gently rub it, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring by their work abscess and contraction to the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at a point, properly restrain the pain that it does not move, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not at a point, and it should be placed in the proper position so that it feels no pain; and ensure that it is placed correctly, as twisting will not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The broken members are different in size, greatness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with soft linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as the thigh and leg: if they are thick, cover them with a wide and strong cloth, for the wide cloths embrace the whole member evenly, so that there is no gap; then wrap lightly around the affected part, three or four times according to the length of the member, and hold your hand a little on every part of the cloth, then go above the break and hold it less, than the break slowly moves away from the break; then soften the cloth a little and a little, until you feel a large part of the sound flesh, then take another cloth, and return immediately below the broken part; then go to the part away from the break, and hold it evenly, not too hard or too painfully, as we have said in the first lesson above; then put between the cloths linen or cloth strips, until they are all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made fingers on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, place something soothing on the abscess, and what opens the abscess, and leave it in place for some time; then place it on the wounds, and be of a moiety of a wide strip, cleanly cut, or of a stick made into brushes, or of palm fronds, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the strip that one places on the wound should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the limb is small or large; then place the strips as you did in the first line, then tie them tightly, as you did in the first line above the wound; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be a medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and be of linen cloth; for if the strips are thick, as I have seen in some works of the threads that make up the cords of linen tapestry, and this is great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and should only have about a quarter of an inch space between each strip.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the hairs are broken by the sharpness of the stars after the straining in their places, put out of them the stains of linen or other clean cloth, so that it does not become a wound.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the broken bones, and the splints are broken, I will tell you about the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is not necessary to strain all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put splints on them until after five or seven days, or more depending on your safety from abscess; and see the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and you take flour that is held as in the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant water, and put this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and it is the common method of the restoring plaster for many positions, and especially to women and small children, because it is not too hard or too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take alabaster, ladanum, enulet, and asafetida, each 1 X; myrrh and aloes, each 5 Z; alechil, 8 Z. Grind them into a powder, mix with honey; if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it quickly heals broken bones, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for sprains: take mugwort and valerian, each 1 X; myrrh and aloes, each 8 Z; bolic armenic, 10 Z. Grind them well, mix with vinegar or honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method to treat joints and bones that are dislocated or broken, to relieve pain, and to use the bone for healing, and the fracture: take new linen, moisten it in oil and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not heal immediately, but they are good for relieving pain from abscesses and properly addressing the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to heal broken bones: take fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a bandage.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method to heal bone fractures and to alleviate the remaining pain from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of valerian, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each one a part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are chilled, mix with mustard or dry mustard.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster, besides the first, when an abscess is about to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of valerian, and linseed, balm, mint, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one a part; and grind, and mix with salt, or sweet mustard, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it with wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it with dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat an injury and pain: take mallow and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and smash them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then release the joint a little later, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, or if the bones of the limb are not misaligned; then do not release it by force again. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or swelling, quickly release it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light bandage, and moisten with fresh mercury, and soak in hot water, and lift the limb until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in hot oil or rose oil, and tie with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and relieve the pain, then restart the subtle bandage, and a little poultice, and do not strain it too much as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is red and hot and painful and swollen, and you have skill in plastering and bandaging, then reapply them as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb within three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, as long as the fracture is present, and approach the splint from above; then hold it more than initially, and increase its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the limb is dryer than it should be, then every time you apply the splint, pour hot water on it, and loosen the bandage a little; by this method, then the swelling is reduced in the limb, and it is quickly remedied as the foolish ones do, who restore the limb incorrectly: this is bad, and if this is not done carefully, and only correctly, I see nothing else but weakness and the work must be done properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking methods
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many breaking methods and various figures, and the causes are distinct; for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the shoulder collapses the entire bone just below the bone, as it does in a hack or a cut; and because of this, this method of breakage is called "hacking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above, piercing it, and this method of breakage is called "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two breaks, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact, or puncture, or from the shoulder of a stone, or to fall on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a break that is persistent, which approaches just at the thread that is dislocated from the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set in the bone as subtly as some hair, and it is the fracture small, and because of this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound that is made or by striking with an arrow, or by falling, or by similar things, and makes the piece of the bone below enter, and is like the nails when they are driven through the radiators; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more who have both wet bones, such as the child's; and they have all these ways of fracture that small pieces are removed like these; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fracture by removal above them, and inquiry with probes, and by the rotten wood that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when the bone is revealed and rubbed with it, if there is an open fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, be careful of the bad accident, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and palsy, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for recovery, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractured bone comes first to you, and it is in ice, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in a state of putrefaction, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the flesh around the bone has not rotted, and the injuries we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fractured bone comes just to the skin that covers the skull, then you must do the following: and it is that you grip the head of the painful wound, and expose it in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with soft cloths soaked in red oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and make sure that the blood does not come out; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and out of position, it is necessary that you pierce around it, as long as you administer cuts with probes, not too far past the jawbone, and should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each side of the bone has a probe; and this is the form of the three methods of probing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for pricking around the broken bone are that you put a sharp object near the bone, and turn it to your right until you feel that the bone is pierced; then remove the sharp object on another part slightly later, and thus do all around, then chip away the space between the bones of the bone which is between the teeth, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone in your hand, or to any of the tools that you have like tongs, pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is advisable to widen the space between the bones of the bone that remains on all other tools similar to an incisor, but it must be more tense and more subtle than the other incisor; and if nothing of the small bones, or scales, remains, remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Galienics say, which is more safe; and it is very good, and that is their word.
