Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can insert the lens-shaped piece of this incisor, which is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the broken piece is in two parts, so that the cutter is against the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, lightly cut the bone, because one cuts well without harming, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth that roughness, and remove scales with the fine razor that you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb as conveniently as possible, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have great razors beforehand, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair clippers and fracture, it is necessary that you manage according to its advancement; and this is a thing that is not immediately answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is discovered, it is necessary that you take a piece of linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another piece of linen doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first piece of cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by means of a bandage, and do not strain it except until the wound is healed; leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess has been calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and administer liquids without bitterness; keep the wound clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor leave any pus, because when pus gathers on the brain, it causes inflammation and pain; for when something is placed on the wound that is bitter, it does not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, as if no accidents come to the limb, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no harm comes to it except by the medicine that has been placed on it, which has its own virtue, then you must apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it in the manner of curing that is suitable, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Be careful that the two bones above the nose are never broken, or one of them alone, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous, and does not break easily, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small finger or nail of the thumb, and put the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the bone regrows according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and keep that the hairs do not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot reach the finger, it is necessary that you put it on the head of a pin or slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the broken part is from both parts, make another and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; if not, after the seventh or twelfth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then break at the head of the finger with pieces of linen cloth, if the broken part is in one piece.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you are applying pressure to one side or the other, where the fracture is, and the bandages are so large that they fill the pores of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no one should moisten the bandages in the morning and evening.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think it is right, but they should be moistened with a mixture of egg and powdered chalk; then leave the bandage until the bone is firm and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feathers in place of bandages, and if there is a wound around the sore, and if the fracture is present, and blow the bad air away; now do what you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put a piece of cotton or cotton wool soaked in rose oil or a drop of iodine into it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess does not come to the nose, apply a poultice made of mustard flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light cotton strips over it and do not tie the nose tightly; if the broken piece of the nose is small and breaks into smaller pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then clean the wound, and treat other injured parts as appropriate, and apply suitable emplastrums and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with bandages and put in hot compresses until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of mandible fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured, and there is no wound except for it, and the fracture is not completely separated, but is broken into two pieces, because of the teeth inside, if one knows this clearly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part, you should press your left index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, press your right index finger, and press the fracture gently inside, and hold it with the other hand by default, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is in two, then you must administer traction of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or breakage, then strain them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place the broken jawbone on a piece of cloth, and place a double cloth over it; and place a large, well-made stele or a piece of leather even and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth so you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the position changes, then release it to the animal, and then put back what was changed; and place a plaster on top, of flour from the mill with an abundance of egg or wheat flour, after you have removed the broken piece; and place the plaster over the plaster, and if the plaster sticks, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come up, as we have often said, apply what we have advised.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, cover no part of the bone that is exposed; rather, carefully cover it with convenient instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have exposed all these pieces and there is none left, dress the wound, if it is wide, by applying convenient poultices to it, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the frog
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways: either it is broken and disfigured into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work when it comes to the fracture with a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one of them holds the forceps broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then put the fracture in your hands, so that it forms as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have to extend further, place the shoulder bone against the pain, using a round cloth ball of cloth or linen, and as large as your need; stretch and relieve the tendon, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you can align the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the tendon of the shoulder outwards, because it comes from above, then it is necessary to prick the painful part over its surface, and place against the middle ear, and push up the shoulder bone until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply pressure to the wound, and if you find broken teeth, it is necessary that you cut above; and carefully remove the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, take one of your sharp instruments; but put the forceps of this instrument aside to guard against the sphincter:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should be as wide as the bone needs, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, one wide and the other narrow, as the rent in the wound that you made when you removed the bones; and when you are sure there is no abscess, close the wound, and if the rent is small, or you doubt an abscess, apply dressing and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come, if you squeeze it, dip a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is in pain and in cut, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the mill powder and some egg, and put on it. Then take a very large bandage of a palm wide, then put the cloth double over the light dressings, and the plaster; then take a subtle staff of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the staff on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the collar, and away from the fracture healthy, and away from the fracture bad; and wrap each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the staff evenly, and you see clearly that the staff does not move over the broken bone, if you reward every day, and when the ligaments are healed, if you restrain it; and make the bad lie on his back, and put what you have when he sleeps a small bandage away from the fracture, to raise the dislocation in the top; if it will align the shoulder by the alignment of the space, or you tie the arm to the neck, and not the disliar if bad accidents do not come, up to XX days; then recommend the plaster, if you see that there is a matter, and strain and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most in XXVIII days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder fractures or is dislocated from its place, and it only occurs by touch; if the splint according to the figure of the fracture, and the arm is put back in its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with abundant water on the limb, and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top; then put a wide and delicate board on top, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the board is not touching any part of the shoulder, use a piece of linen to make it even; and then tightly bind the whole with a strong bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the bone every day; and every time it breaks, tighten the bandage, and if the board is broken, replace it, and ease the pain on its side; and the shoulder is healed in 20 or 30 days, and when this number is completed, remove the bandages, and be careful, for it is not bones that are put back firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of bone is felt to be broken before the joint, and not moved from its place, then cut above it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the finger's joint to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the little finger
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The little finger is never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the base.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it turns outwards, and causes great pain, and disability, and all, and perhaps blood is vomited, and the jaw opens in the broken bone, and it feels very bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the hairs are pushed back over their heads, and the hand is placed between the shoulder blades, then the shoulder blades are pressed, and the ribs of the two ribcages are brought together in your hands, and subtly placed evenly in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and soft salves or other light ones on the thin bone, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; then gently round the limb back to its place, gradually tighten it, and rub the book on it every hour, and if it moves, tighten it again; and if it is necessary to loosen it due to corrosion or itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hasten, loosen it, and remove the bandage, and apply what has come from methods of healing; then reapply the bandage, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fractures of the ribs come only from great blows to the chest and the back, and at the top, and they break only because they are brittle; and the pain is felt well during the examination of this.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the healing is such that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage of a splint, if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, it causes great pain and tingling, as if from pleurisy, because the bones do not touch the lungs; and it should be splinted, and everything and drained a lot of blood, and this is very bad health, and the old ones have put much effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that cause the stomach to swell, in order to push the fragment away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless there is no abscess, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then lance it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that no one puts suction cups on the limb, for they draw out the excess from the limb due to its weakness in position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that no one should cover the limb with linen cloth in warm oil, and then place tents between the ribs to equalize the liquid inside, then treat the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that they cannot bear it due to the bone not being broken, and there is doubt, then you must cut through the rib on the side that is broken, and place a probe to ward off the sinus; and then you must break the bone, and gently pull, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come on the face, place soft cloths soaked in rose oil on the affected area; and treat while the wound lies as it should, lying beside the coste where it is supposed to be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when a breaker breaks bones of the neck, and often it does not rain; and so on the backbone.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you know whether it will be healthy or not, if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is deadly in many positions, and if it moves and feels well when restrained and not, then the joint of the bone is saved, and the wounds are healed, and it is cured.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	If a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, if you take warning when the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and on top of the back suddenly vent and egestion without will; and when they lie on their stomach, if there is sudden egestion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it lies on its back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care for this is that you reward him if he has an abscess that is ready to burst, by placing a red oil or egg yolk on the spine, until it is relieved; then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, and tie it with a bandage, and command him to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dry, it is necessary to cover it with a cloth; then remove the bone, then gather the two ends of the wound, if it is large, at one seam, then treat the wound with a poultice until it is healed; and if the patient's shoulder bone is broken, which is called the "shoulder bone fracture," if you have the ability, put your right hand on the other hand to your power, then place the plaster and the bandage on top, if you have the skill; then strain, and if there is a dry bone, do it again, and remove, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if they are, it does not cause much pain to the head; and making it long, and declining towards the side, and coming to the wrong place, it causes great pain, swelling, and inflammation where the bone is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the broken part; and remove the fragments of the break and its shape; and if the break is only at the top, then set it back into its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long and it leans inwards, lie the patient on their belly until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured bone so it does not move; and treat the wound on both sides, until the joint is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their side or their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms and comes, do not touch it until the abscess is calm, and follow what we have said before; then return to healing, and hold it as it should be, unless there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a single bone grinder, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two broken bones together, and raise them up high, and saw the misaligned part above the seat; then pour some arm bone over the broken part, until it comes to ease, and put a hook of bone in it, then raise it above any heavy thing or the minister extends it down; then put the splint the breaker together with his hands together, until the breaker returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should prick the pain above its surface, and hold the hand on its collar, then command two ministers that one ties what is above the broken part to his hands, and the other ties behind everything, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, hold the tie behind the broken part, and above the broken part, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken part is close to the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place the tie behind the shoulder blade, and the other towards the back, outside the broken part; and similarly if the broken part is towards the back, then it is necessary to place the tie lightly, without labor, until the broken part is even above the shoulder, and above the back, then make it even, as it should be, and stretch it, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it fast for more than seven days, and put on a poultice of milk and rose oil until the abscess is soothed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you place the bandage on the swollen part, then bring the arm up with the assistance of the other, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the dressing on, and hold it with the assistance of the other, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture than the others, and have between each splint two inches of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side; then strain against the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less distantly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the splints and the straining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is not healed, leave it to lie for seven days, as we have said; then examine the joint every three days, that it does not prick or swell, or that the inflammations do not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the joint, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur within three hours or more, the patient should sleep with his back to the pain, and his hands on his stomach; and place a linen cloth evenly over the injury, and check every hour of the day or night that the broken limb does not move, or that the tendons are not softened; if the joint heals by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is very fine; and when he begins to regain strength, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in 40 days after all; and then one should remove and administer warm water and medicinal ointments for the limb to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if its structure is crooked and swollen, it may take 2 months or more to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus," one of which is small, and is that which supports the elbow; and the other is large, and is that which is outside, towards the little finger; occasionally, the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and occasionally both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is best to extend them slightly and align them.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is best to strain them more; and extend them over the cushion, and tuck the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the fingers cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher than the fingers so that they do not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers to the part outside of his hand, or to the elbow, and other ministers to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no suitable bone to hold the tooth, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a bridge and the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken of it to the chapter; take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then use the poultice made of red oil and white wax, which is not too soft or too hard; and tie the poultice gently until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the plaster, and apply the powder from the mill with abundant oil, then place the splints, and set the broken piece back in place, and a little wider than the others; and there should be six or more splints: whether the broken piece is in one of the bones, or in two; and it should be held above the break, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, which is used to hold the break together, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	If any accident occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must raise the limb in hot water, until the itching is relieved; and let the limb rest without being restrained.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then begin the strapping again, and if the limb is softened and the bones are dislocated, or something similar occurs, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the swelling has gone, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to the patient's harm, then let it go for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Then apply the hands to his neck, and make his collar even, and keep him still and warm, and let him sleep on his back; and if this painful part is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, according to the constitutions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Then apply at the back of the hand and to us has little breaking parts, and it comes only many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or splintered, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place your hand on the spread cloth, and extend the bones that are broken, and put them evenly in their places until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is in the web of the hand, make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to hold it against their broken hand; then wrap it with a long piece of cloth, and place the splint as large as the hand of the patient, and hold it in place as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the under side, it is necessary that you put a splint above, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stanch the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers, if it is in the palm, place it evenly as it should be; and strain with the hand, and if you see that you should put a straight small splint to lift the fractured part, and do not move; and if the fracture is on other fingers, such as the index or another, place it evenly, and bind with the sound finger that is next; or you bind all of them together holding, which is best, or you put above a splint, as in the palm; and take care in restoration and position of abscess, and support what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the rib are often broken, and well seen when they return in front and behind; and the restoration is so that one lies above and the other below the broken one.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs are tied above his face, then each minister stretches their string evenly to their part; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the rib, then one of the strings should be on the side of the base, and the other strings outside the broken one.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the glenoid, and then one of the strings should be on the side of the glenoid, and the other string below; then put the bone in your hands evenly according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if there are no more wounds.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess that is boiling, let it cool first, then return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in a similar manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the fractured bone in two or three layers of cloth, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the toes reach the root of the foot, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the end of the thread above; then turn back up the leg and the thigh, and tie the fractured bone with three splints above, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to equalize the tension, then begin to bandage around three or four times above the fracture; and as you go higher than the fracture, and less the tension; then examine the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three splints above, then return to the top of the thread, until you reach below the knee joint; and if it does not move from its place, then let it remain, so that there is no abscess or swelling of any other kind.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, remove the dislocation, and return it to its place as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that can be felt, they should be removed if possible; and if not, the limb should be cut and pulled out; and the cure is as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And the ribs are never broken in this way as when the arm or shoulder is dislocated; however, in the restoration done in this way does not cause pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is said that the ribs are restored in different times, according to the variations of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the street of the gentleman there is little damage, but it rains often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and it feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its two, as long as it can be assembled well; then put the plaster, and if you have skill, put a round splint, and hold it as it should be, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other breaks, such as abscess and similar things; put to each accident what it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right, and the other is called "foscile"; and they break equally as in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken at once, then the leg returns to all its parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it returns outwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, relieve the extension, and make it even, and tie the wounds equally; but nonetheless, it is necessary to break the fracture if it is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and bind it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that bind the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to cover the leg from the knee down to the ankle; then wrap it around the leg above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long strip of cloth on the leg, and if it is made properly, and they put the leg to prevent movement, and properly done, they move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the skull
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but of the bones of the skull, there is never a fracture and it does not break, and there are only a few dislocations in certain positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the skull, and you see these bones overlapped on top of each other, if they are protruding from the ground, like they want to walk, then put your foot on the spot where the bones are raised, then press them so much that they return to their place; then apply the plaster and wipe the wound, and put a small pad on the forehead of the patient, then strap the head evenly, then wrap bandages around it and other things that you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the joint, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, then restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and it should be slightly wider, then put the bandage as I have described, and strain evenly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and strain the bandage from outside the bone; and let it be above the head of the bone under the belly of the wound, so that it heals well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other injuries, as soon as we have mentioned them; and provide care for each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are fractured, if the pain is widespread, then lean her back, and tilt her to the side, and hold her from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then raise the woman, and slowly lift her up, and gradually remove the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bones return with the cotton; and when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has done so, replace it, and thus do this for seven days or so: if it is restored, and if you see, take a bladder of goose fat, and tie a cloth around it, and blow all the fat into the wound; then blow into the cloth forming a ball, until the fat is inflated inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in place for some time, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the tooth of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these broken teeth are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into this book, and pays attention to it.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the broken tooth signifies many different positions of the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the finger, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert it into the finger; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone with a fracture and wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleaned immediately, so that the cleanings we have mentioned are testified to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if there is no other thing, then restart to restore the fractured part in the same hour, or the next day, if it becomes infected.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if infection comes, then leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the infection is calmed down, and do not touch it on the next day or the fourth, for you will bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the jaw is broken and appears to be displaced, then it is necessary to gently place your fingers on it, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not match your hand, then use this iron instrument which is made of iron, which has seven or eight inches long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this reason, it should be three or four times as thick as the thickness of the limb at your work, and it should be round and a little thick, so that it does not press too much against the member at your work, and it should be narrow in front and wide in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient should have the broken bone placed above the top of the visible bone; and it is bound once, as much as it reunites, and they are evenly aligned one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the instruments cannot well take the bone, then you must cut off the top of the bone until the instruments have a hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then use a suitable tool, such as a saw or chisel, to your ability; then scrape off what remains in the bone of sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned to its place, and the pain is great afterwards, do not let it stay in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do this until it is in its natural position, then moisten the bandage with stiff black wine, and properly if it was already there; and do not put anything else on the wound except oil, where it has oil, so that it does not bring about putrefaction and corruption; then administer these things as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not pressed with the fracture; and many times this has been done by fools, and they have caused the pain or death or corrosion of any time; and let the strain be gentler and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that it is not a bad accident as we have said, and you try to move the limb but it causes pain, then do not put anything on top of it; instead wrap it around, in place of the bandage, with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is closing, remove what you have placed on top of it at all times, and put on a healing ointment, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to move the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be aligned in such a way that the bow moves easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue for too long, and it cannot be mended but remains bent, because there are small pieces of bone, therefore it is necessary that you remove the wound with a tent, and take out all those unnecessary pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if the fistula comes to the limb, or in another way of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bones of the shoulder or the arm, and other similar large members, do not remove it immediately, for many times it kills, but let it remain until it can be healed; perhaps it will fall off after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of sudden blows that come to the injury
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of the broken bone, exactly at the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the misalignment of the limb; and perhaps it cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if we find it fresh: then administer stiffening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and marrow, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, so that you include none of these things, or all together, and mix them with stiffening wine or with abundant honey or with garlic; and place it on the nose in a plug, and hold it tightly, and do not leave it in the hand for long; then remove it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you hold against a piece of lead well made; because the property of the lead is that it removes all the swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the cope above, and make the excess apparent; or you cut it with any razor, until it is removed, and care until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after surgery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and remains after the limbs are weak and subtle, there are many causes for this: one is because it was tied too tightly and not loosened as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not reach the members to the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and give baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the swelling often of high heat, as long as the swelling goes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a deformed limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not harm its natural appearance: thus one should not believe those who say that one must break the limb entirely in new, and many have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harms come from it, and perhaps death; however, if the fractures and twists are fresh, then it is necessary to apply heating or softening herbs that have been boiled, such as willow bark, roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as well-made diluted oil of poppy, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose grease or poppyseed oil, and apply the plaster on; or you take figs, and grind them with flour of linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And it is often necessary to apply continuous and prolonged pressure with dry hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you should gently move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awake and hard, like stone, and it needs to be cut with a knife, if it is necessary to cut into the bone, with a thin and subtle incision; and put ointment and rest in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
