Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be brought back against the shoulder blade.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if the shoulder swells, and perhaps if it is reset to the bone; for it does not matter that one moves it to where it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains; however, when it will be over, if you make the pain go away, then leave the limb, until the abscesses are soothed; then raise the limb with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare that the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocation of the jaws occurs in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and prevent the saliva from the mouth from being held, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its place in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if she is whole and complete, it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the minister sterilizes the head of the dislocation, and places the fingers of one hand at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is outside, to hold even; and command the dislocation to soften its jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers should be equal until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both jaws are together, raise the tips of high hot oil, and do not delay in resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned evenly, and the jaw with the bad tooth is well closed to soften, put a cloth soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on it, then lightly bandage it with moist bindings; let the pains lie on its back, and its jaws be between two cushions, so that it does not move to the left or right, nor strive much to chew, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaw is healed; then change what it wants lightly, and do not strain much to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour and are not converted back to their usual alignment, then it may lead to fevers and sweating, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is a sign of danger; and many times the one who has it dies within fourteen days.
de la forcelle	of force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be used from the side of the chest without causing damage to the body, and it is not reset once dislocated, and well one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the dislocated limb is gently brought back to its place on one's back, and extends its arms; then press the limb firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the bandage and the binder, and hold it in place; and the patient who is lying on their side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the bandage and the binder, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until it is healed; and thus the same is done with the shoulder when it is healed from its injury.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	of the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: the first is that it is dislocated at the part of the armpit to the outside; and the second is at the part of the elbow; and sometimes at the part above, and this is rare; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it is dislocated outwards towards the armpit, especially to those who have little strength, because to these it is done harshly; to those who have enough strength, it is done gently, and it returns gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men have pressure or fractures, and the shoulder swells with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must first examine him to be sure; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation is when it is down towards the shoulder, and it distinguishes between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find a difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and outside the shoulder, the top of the shoulder, like if it were a bone; and it cannot move its hand to its neck, or move any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated in the top, it is not hidden, because you will see it clearly outside; and this way of dislocation is only to be put back, when it is new, or if there are pains.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the attendant lifts the badly affected hand upwards, then places the fingers outside the joint, and pulls the joint upwards to the shoulder; and the attendant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, then it is necessary that the affected hand be soaked in hot water; and the attendant should apply a softening and moistening remedy, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it; then the affected hand should be placed on its back, and a piece of cloth equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed outside the joint, then the palm of the hand should be placed on top of the cloth, and the shoulder should be lifted virtuously, and the attendant should pull the affected hand; and another attendant should wet the head of the affected hand, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now all right, and if you see that the dislocation is corrected according to this method: and it is necessary that you show the person who is larger than the affected hand; and he should be on the side of the chest, and pull the shoulder of the affected hand away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the affected hand hangs in the air; and another attendant should take the affected hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, with it can be anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting can also be done in another way: and it is that one puts a long thin stick in the ground, which the patient should also hold like a dart, and it should not be too thick or too rough; then it should be placed outside of the pain, but with cloth underneath, and the pain should be on the long end of the stick; then the hand should be extended from the other side, forming a shape, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if all these things we have said do not make it return, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms in width and four fingers in length, which has the head rounded for muscles to enter from the outside, like this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie it above the shoulder with soft cloth, which was not too tight and caused the pain, then remove it from the side of the pain; and extend one arm over the long one, and tie the helper over the long one, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm over the wide end of a spoon, and let the hands hang down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in whatever way it may be, it is necessary to put a cloth of even wool on the side, then apply the plaster with powder from the mill, with incense and some oil, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove it from the side gradually, and return the joint to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change it little, until the limbs are comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then change it again after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is stiff and does not become soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is very strong due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cautery at three points, as it is placed before or in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot be raised above the shoulder, then cut the nerves at the head of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the back, and the shoulders, or behind, is caused by impact, and extension of hands, and there is another remedy administered; and cure until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member becomes stiff and moves slowly, then use the hairs many times in baths until that stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the shoulder joint is dislocated at the points, and repeatedly returns; and it is dislocated from all parts, and specifically in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired, for one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, make sure to see it clearly open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is cut, and cannot swell the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the joint as soon as the swelling comes, for if the swelling comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset completely at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, but still causes great pain, and perhaps it kills.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is so that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to both of their hands; and their arms are spread out, and their hands on either side of the joint, outside and inside, and push the joint together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the place, then administer strong extension; and it is that those who extend the arm, and hold the arm extended by two people, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when the eye sees the joint at the hand, if there is any oil to soften the joint, then bolt the joint together, as much as it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and hold it in place, and put the arm on the back of the bad shoulder, and leave it for some time, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then dislocate it and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the bandage and the limb, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly placed; then dislocate it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If it feels gritty after the readjustment of the joint and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or put a thick piece of fat lamb on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and put it in bath water; and when it sweats, rub the joint immediately, then put the fat back on, and then put it in bath water; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then put a piece of moist, warm chaff with butter on it, and strain it; it will return to its original position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it should be quickly returned to its place at the same moment it is dislocated, provided that the limb is swollen or there is an abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is that you place the misaligned hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and the mirror places it evenly so that the palm is placed over the appearance of the joint, and the pressure is applied until it returns. Therefore, it is necessary to check if it is properly in place; then place the hairs on the back of the hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's back of their hand on a table, and the doctor places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns, it is well. If not, apply calming ointments to the abscess and let it rest before starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot be borne, and you cannot place it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; do not force anything into the patient's hand until it is washed, and nothing can be forced into it: then cut the tendon or artery; otherwise, there is no other remedy except to apply cauterization through the skin, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is dislocated, put the poultice that we have said above on it, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no swelling, then apply hot water to the affected area, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The two fingers of the hand are not dislocated at any part, not at the back of the palm or the belly; therefore, hold the head of the finger, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for three days, and then put it in place that day; and bind it as we have said, and remove the bandage the next day, and move it, and realign it; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	back dislocation of the shoulder
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder joint or neck joint is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the egestions suddenly jump out of volition, cannot be held, and often soften any member, or the two forearms or the right arm or one; often the shoulder moves at an angle; this is called "gibbousness"; the cure is to reward the gibbousness if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that fall or are caused by impacts or similar things, they said in the old ways of healing with great words, but I have abbreviated them according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the back, there is no engineering or health; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure otherwise than that proper one which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the limbs should be stretched out evenly on his face in the first joint, and he should have some strain away from him, so that he does not become swollen; then make the bandage at the head in a proper way, and the other at the feet, and tie one bond outside the limbs of the injured part, and the other as the hips, and as the knees, and as the ankles; and the assistant should secure the bonds, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well fastened, the bandage as we have said, and the fingers put his palms on the spine properly, until he recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a three-legged stool and twist it off the ground, and the pain should be on one side, and beat the head of the stool away from the ground, then put the middle of the stool on the spine; and place the patient's feet on the other end of the stool, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it to the other side.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fasten two bands to the head of the painful arm of a long arm, and behind the feet two others, and have between each band, inside and outside, a palm of length; and have in each band one hole, where the turner goes, and the bands are firmly on the ground so that they do not move; and between the two bands have one turning band, along with the turner's bands, and have in two turns two small bands of a length of palm, to turn the turner; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the turner's head, and the other ligament to the feet of the other turner, and each minister turns his turner along the whole ligament, and the masters put the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a desiccating plaster with abundant honey, then soak it, then place it on a tablet of three inches length, which supports the neck of the spine and the part of the spine that is healthy, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until it is healed; and if nothing comes at the end of health, then administer medicines that are softening and astringent, with the same tablet that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never come to appear in the back spine of the back, and beware that this is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which we should not have any presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Although the joints of the hip and shoulder do not come out only as dislocations, but also as other joints; and the hip joint is misaligned in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than that, and slightly misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is such that when the injured leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy one, and cannot bend its knee to the fire; and it is the ones that are swollen on the inside because of an abscess, for the reason that the wound in the groin comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has this before are that he is well-aligned with his leg according to completion; however, if there is double knee pain, and if it is wanted to make it move forward, it cannot be done before, and retains urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has this behind are that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated at the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this kind of dislocation are such that if it is old, and it stays according to its position, there is no cure; and it is not necessary that it has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this kind where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, you must quickly return the joint, and stretch it from inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, and there is no other treatment needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare one strong minister, and stretch the leg firmly at two joints, or at one that is tied above the knee; and other ministers extend their hand under in such a way that they bite their hands away from their elbows, then strangle him with a rope lying across his back; and some tie the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must care for its similarity. When the dislocation is at the patella, then you should feel the pain above the knee, then place the ligament on the root of the patella, and the leg that is off the angle, then extend the ligament above the angle and towards the calf; then take other ministers to grasp the thick ligament of the misaligned knee, and extend it in the proper form: it will return to its leg now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not manage to hold the two legs of the dislocated shoulder together in this manner that we have described, it is necessary that you tie the two hairs of the painful part together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the painful leg be stretched out two fingers more than the other; then hang it suspended by the chief of a stick, and let it hang off the ground two arms' length; then command the minister to grasp the back of the shoulder, and another minister to hold the dislocated part, who should form the back of the shoulder, for the joint is now beginning to return.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the lower part, grasp the painful part, as we have said in the one with gout, and hold the joint above the painful leg properly, and also above the foot; then put two bands, one at the head and the other at the foot, then tie the band between the thighs on the painful part, to keep it in place; and wrap moist cloths around, so it does not become stiff, then stretch each assistant towards him, and the mirror put equal to his hand, the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the flat surface, and press it as we have said in gout, and grasp the painful part on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to extend the injured leg firmly, and as I have said; and place the fingers of your pain above the misaligned joint, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the injured leg downwards, nor to raise it up, but it should be as it was aligned when it was dislocated from behind, as we have said about the position of the two hips; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be in place when the leg is extended, and they will be even; then bend the knees, and put the plaster, and the bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release it, and put the plaster on again; and if you see that they are even, tighten the bandage, as before, and leave it for three days; then release it, and make the limb move well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: to wit, from within and without, and from behind; and it does not dislocate from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he cannot do so at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on yours; then take his shoulder to your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can lightly bend his leg at the knee; and put the plaster on, and support the leg against the knee, and tie them together very tight for three or four hours, then release it; and do not work on the patient any more until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never sprained and never fully dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is dislocated, and it feels painful when touched at the part where it is dislocated: the movements are light, and one should gently extend it to their hands when it is sprained only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, one should sit the bone straight, and hold it with the hands, above the ankle; then pull the tendon to your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and strike the tendon loudly in the upper part; and do this twice, as we have said, pulling and pushing the tendon; if it returns, it is well; if not, if you restart the work, it will return; and if it cannot return like this, then make the bone lie on its back on the ground, and fix the splint firmly in the earth between the thighs, and wrap cloths around, so that it does not move the bone; then hold the hands of the assistant on the thigh, and another assistant extend the tendon to their hands or to the ligament, so that they can hold the tendon while stretching; then stretch each assistant equally, and the splints should be placed between the thighs of the dislocated bone to hold it while stretching; then put the hands equal to the dislocation at your hands, and another assistant hold the leg clean on the outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she does not go away, put the plaster and wipe above, and let the swelling form, and tie the foot to the leg, and hold the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints are not too stretched; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling does not decrease, take away the plaster; then let it go to the next day or the fourth, and defend against the pain for four days; and if it goes before that term, it is not sure that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you relieve it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they should be extended well towards work, and this is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no part of the joint, then it is necessary to make the patient sit with the painful part above the flat or straight table, and put your foot on what opens these joints, then press strongly on your foot until it returns; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, then remove the sole of the foot from the table, place it on a second table at the elbow, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocations, and one wants to restore them, often times the pain causes death: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and you are not knowledgeable in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and slow, nor hardhearted; at the beginning of things, gently treat abscesses, and leave the pain in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place, as soon as the abscesses have passed; and when the member is in place, administer remedies for abscesses, and treat the wound, as it should be, with dry dressings; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are crushed, remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
Amen	For the fire cautery
